1936.06.16

Southwestern Faction Discusses Post-Withdrawal Issues; Will Send Representatives to the Second Plenary Session; Two Regiments of the Guangxi Army Remain Stationed in Yongzhou Awaiting Orders; Situation in Hengzhou Indeed Trending Toward Conciliation

(Hong Kong) The Executive Department held a meeting on the morning of the 15th to discuss all issues after the troop withdrawal. Security was extremely tight. It is rumored that one or two key members will be sent to attend the Second Plenary Session. Li Xiangen from the Political Council will arrive in Hong Kong on the 16th to urge Tang Shaoyi to go to the province. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Li Bai replied to various parties on the 15th, stating that he had ordered his troops to make concessions. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Zhang Renmin flew from Yongzhou to Guangdong on the 15th to report to Li on his meeting with Bai. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Wang Xunzhi said on the 15th that the Guangdong Army had retreated to Chenzhou, while two regiments of the Guangxi Army remained stationed in Yongzhou awaiting orders. Miao Peinan returned to headquarters on the 15th to work, and Yu Hanmou attended the joint memorial week on the morning of the 15th. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Changsha) He Jian reported during the memorial week on the 15th that Hunan province is safe, urging everyone to remain calm and maintain normalcy. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Today, the Joint Association of Secondary and Higher Education Schools telegraphed Chen, Xiao, Huang, Li, Bai, etc., in the Southwest, urging them to pull back from the brink and preserve the nation's vitality, and requested Chiang to find a way to stop the civil war. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Political Council decided to send Li Xiangen to Hong Kong again to strongly invite Tang Shaoyi to continue as a standing committee member. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Zhang Renmin arrived in Guangdong by plane from Guangxi at 1 PM on the 15th to visit Chen and Li, reporting on the military situation in Guangxi. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Hengzhou The main force of the Guangxi Army is still in the Yongzhou and Qiyang area. The troops that retreated from east of Qiyang are still constructing defensive positions in the Lingguan Temple and Xiongzhiling area of Qiyang. Their rear units are continuing to concentrate forward, and they claim they will not stop until they reach Changsha. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Hengzhou Since the Southwest Army withdrew to the Hunan border, the situation in Hengzhou has indeed become much calmer. It is rumored that the Southwest authorities and the Central Government are currently engaged in negotiations. The future situation will depend on the outcome of these peace talks. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

(Hankou) When Dr. Green, an employee of the Changsha Christian Church, arrived here today, a Reuters reporter interviewed him. He stated that the Southwest Army's withdrawal from Hunan began last Thursday. The overall situation is gradually becoming calmer, and merchants in Changsha are no longer worried. The British Consulate in Changsha had ordered female employees of churches in outer counties to gather in the provincial capital last week, but many have now returned to their original posts. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Today's editorial in The Times stated that Westerners know very little about China's custom of warfare. Although South China and the Central Government are now at risk of civil war, the news received is extremely brief, and we need not waste time speculating. However, this situation is partly due to important economic reasons. Even if it can be rectified today to avoid trouble, it will still erupt one day. It would be surprising if the various factors driving the South China side did not include an element of anti-Japanese sentiment, unlike many events in Asia today that are made in Japan. It is an underestimation of the Chinese people's primary intelligence to believe that the Southern Army will engage in a serious war with the Central Army in order to force the Central Government to engage in a serious war with Japan. The dispute between the two sides will not be resolved by warfare. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) Yu Hanmou and Miao Peinan both attended the memorial week meeting this morning, which is enough to dispel rumors that they were under house arrest. Yu addressed the crowd, stating that the Guangdong Army in Hunan province had retreated to Chenzhou and Lechang, which proves the Southwest's obedience to the central government's orders. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) The Southwest Army has completely withdrawn from Hunan province to the Guangdong border. The differences of opinion between Guangzhou and Nanjing must await the Second Plenary Session to be held on July 10 to resolve. At the same time, Southwest leaders are now discussing the policies they need to take in the future. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

(Guangzhou) In the past few days, the Southwest Army has been withdrawing from Hunan province and still needs to continue to complete it. It is reported that the Guangxi Army is now concentrated in Yongzhou, 15 miles inside the Hunan border, and the Guangdong Army is now concentrated in Bangzhou, 20 miles inside the Hunan border. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Chen Weizhou went to Hong Kong on the 12th to persuade Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai to cooperate. It is rumored that Jiang and Cai requested that the 19th Route Army be restored and provided with salaries and weapons. Chen from Guangdong only promised to help as appropriate and promised to issue a mobilization fee of 50,000 yuan immediately, but Jiang and Cai must gather their troops and wait for orders to depart before the 24th. Chen Weizhou returned to the province on the 14th and will come again to negotiate. (15th Shen Shi News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) A certain party provided the Guangdong-Guangxi armies with 15 aircraft. The aircraft parts were disguised as cement and the wings were disguised as large iron sheets in Taiwan, then transported to Hong Kong and transferred to the province. The Aviation Department has sent personnel to Hong Kong to inspect and accept them. (15th Shen Shi News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Military and political figures gathered at Xiao Focheng's residence on the morning of the 14th to secretly discuss countermeasures to deal with the current situation. It is rumored that Li Zongren still advocates for a radical approach, which will be decided by the Political Committee meeting on the 16th. It is rumored that the government may propose it. (15th Shen Shi News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Political Council held a meeting on the morning of the 15th to discuss various matters. The content was very secret, but according to reliable sources, Chen, Li, and Bai still advocate for war. They have been stepping up their defense preparations in recent days while expressing conciliation to the outside world. They also plan to send Chen Weizhou north to confess everything to the central government. (15th Shen Shi News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) After the changes in the Guangdong Army, military expenses are enormous. Construction and education funds have been completely diverted, but it is still not enough. Therefore, it has been decided to issue 10 million yuan of anti-Japanese war bonds in the short term. (15th Shen Shi News Agency Dispatch)

Guangzhou Japanese Consul Protests to Guangdong Authorities

(Guangzhou) The Japanese Consul here, Kawakami, lodged a serious protest with the Chinese authorities today regarding the anti-Japanese movement in Guangdong province, paying particular attention to the large-scale anti-Japanese demonstration in Guangzhou on June 13. He stated that such actions would greatly affect Sino-Japanese relations, and the Japanese government considers this parade to be in violation of the principles of Sino-Japanese friendship. The Chinese authorities have not yet responded, but the Japanese consul's protest has made the public uneasy, fearing that it will lead to new Sino-Japanese negotiations in South China. At the same time, according to Chinese sources, the situation in Shantou is also very chaotic due to the friction between China and Japan, and developments there are now being closely watched here. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

Sangajima Visits Song Zheyuan

Exchanges Views on North China Issues; Song and Qin Host Separate Banquets

(Beiping) Sangajima, accompanied by Shimizu, a counselor from the Japanese Embassy, visited Song this morning to exchange views on the North China issue. The meeting lasted for one hour, and then he left to visit Qin Dechun at the Municipal Government for a routine courtesy call. Qin hosted a banquet for Sangajima at the Municipal Government at noon, inviting Shui, Okuda, and Chen Juesheng to accompany him. Tonight, Song will host a banquet for Sangajima at the Diplomatic Building. Members of the Political Committee and the Foreign Affairs Committee, as well as key embassy staff from the Japanese Embassy, ​​have been invited to accompany him. Sangajima is scheduled to fly to Zhangjiakou tomorrow morning with Shimizu for inspection, and is scheduled to return to Beiping that evening and then go to Jinan. (15th Special Dispatch)

Ronin Riot Disorderly; Forcibly Demand Vehicles to Transport Smuggled Goods

(Tianjin) At 3 PM on the 15th, dozens of Korean ronin surrounded the office of Chief Mao of the Beining East Station Freight Department, demanding that Mao attach southbound freight cars on the Jinpu Railway for the transportation of special trade items such as sugar and rayon. Mao was forced to comply and, along with seven representatives, went to the Beining Railway Bureau, where they were received by Zhou Qingman, the director of the car department. The ronin rioted disorderly. Liu Shaokun was dispatched to the Japanese Consulate to invite Deputy Consul Nishida, who led several police officers, accompanied by two Japanese inspectors from the Beining Railway Police Department, Shimoura and Mikyo, to take the ronin away. These ronin are members of the Sugar Special Trade Association formed a few days ago, unable to bear the losses. Based on a resolution passed on the 14th, they made unreasonable demands to the railway administration. At 9 AM on the 15th, on the southbound passenger train No. 74 on the Jinpu Railway, there were more than 30 ronin carrying firearms, forcibly occupying four carriages, loading more than 800 pieces of sugar, rayon, and cigarette paper. The railway administration temporarily stopped the train and persuaded them to unload, but the ronin refused. Customs officials dared not approach them. After a long delay, they were finally allowed to transport the goods, and passengers were squeezed to the point where there was no room to stand. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) A trainload of smuggled white sugar arrived today without paying the freight. The railway administration refused to accept it because demanding fees would be tantamount to admitting smuggling. The Anti-Smuggling Department ordered the railway police to detain it. Later, some Koreans drove more than ten cars with a certain country's flag inserted, forcibly transporting it away. The railway police were injured, and one person was taken away, and a car was pushed off in the middle of the road. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) 3,780 packages of smuggled goods were transported from Tianjin to Jinan today, including rayon, cloth, and cigarette paper, especially sugar. (15th Special Dispatch)

British MP Questions North China Smuggling

Investigation Awaits in the Case of Murder of Japanese Officer

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden stated in the House of Commons today in response to a question from Conservative MP Moring that the British government has repeatedly raised questions with the Japanese government regarding smuggling in North China, and the British government will continue to take any action it deems beneficial in the future. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) British Foreign Secretary Eden, at the request of Conservative MP Moore, announced the circumstances of the case in which the Japanese authorities accused guards of the British Embassy in Beiping of beating to death Japanese military officer Sasaki. After Foreign Secretary Eden described the origins of the case, he stated that the resolution of the investigation court, which confirmed the results of the initial investigation, was sent to the Japanese Embassy, ​​which then presented the testimony of several Koreans, who now claim to recognize three guards from the British Embassy who participated in some disturbance on the night of the murder. At the same time, the investigation is still ongoing, and the witnesses will be summoned by the investigation court. Conservative MP MacDonald asked on what grounds the Japanese accused British soldiers of committing the crime. The Foreign Secretary replied that the case is currently being handled by the investigation court and that it should be awaited until it is adjudicated. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

Tianjin Japanese Military Department Holds Meeting; Exchanges Views on the Current Situation Centered on Nagami; Closely Monitors the Two Guangdong Provinces and Seizes Opportunities to Act

(Tianjin) There was a meeting at the Zhangyuan official residence in the Japanese Concession at 2 PM on the 15th, centered on Nagami. Iida, Ishii, Nakai, Hamada, Ikeda, Kawada, and other majors, as well as the military staff of the garrison headquarters above the rank of major, participated to exchange views on the current situation. It was decided that: 1. The merger of Hebei-Chahar and East Hebei will not be accepted for negotiation for the time being. The status quo of the two regimes will be maintained. 2. Serious attention will be paid to the northward advance of the Southwest, and they will rush to the location as soon as the opportunity arises. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Nagami is scheduled to return to his country on August 8 and will be transferred to a new position. The Chief of Staff of the Japanese Garrison in North China will be replaced by a major general. Recently, all diplomacy in Hebei-Chahar has been presided over by Nagami. Many of those in charge of negotiations on our side have clashed with his opinions. Tashiro is also dissatisfied with Nagami's policies and will inevitably be replaced. Currently, dark clouds are looming, and the authorities are maintaining calmness in the face of the activities of a certain envoy and a certain commander, taking a "seeing is believing" attitude and expecting to resume contact along the right track after the Japanese personnel adjustment. (15th Special Dispatch)

Inns in Tianjin Handles Smuggling Disputes

Solicits Opinions from British and American Merchants; Seeks Independent Methods of Interception

(Tianjin) Inns is soliciting opinions from British and American merchants on the Tianjin anti-smuggling matter, abandoning diplomatic channels and seeking independent methods of interception. Inns himself is supervising the branch offices south of Cangzhou in Tianjin, discovering and adopting rapid interception methods for smuggled goods. In the event of disputes, Inns rushes to handle them. According to customs information, the trend of smuggling south of Zhengzhou on the Pinghan Line is still not rampant, and interception is easier. The Zhengzhou Inspection Branch Office plans to reconsider the situation and make a decision. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Inns is delaying his departure from Tianjin due to the arrangement of anti-smuggling affairs in Tianjin. The Ministry of Finance will send someone else to prepare for the Pinghan Inspection Branch Office, focusing on the Wuzhuang and Baoding areas to prevent smuggling into Henan. (15th Special Dispatch)

Tashiro Banquets Foreign Nationals in Tianjin

(Tianjin) Commander Tashiro hosted a party at the Zhangyuan official residence on the 15th and 16th to celebrate with prominent figures from the British, American, and other countries in Tianjin, as well as members of the press, with more than 30 people attending. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Hamada, the military attache stationed in Beiping, came to Tianjin this morning on the orders of Matsumuro to report to Tashiro on the student movement and to discuss the progress of the meeting with Song. He returned to Beiping in the evening. (15th Special Dispatch)

Xiao Zhenying Resigns; Authorities Are Trying to Retain Him

(Tianjin) Shi Jisheng, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, said that Mayor Xiao's resignation was due to unfavorable circumstances. The authorities are still trying hard to retain him. Last night, someone falsely claimed to be from the Beiping News Inspection Office and notified the Tianjin News Inspection Office to inform various newspapers to publish the news about Zhang Zizhong's appointment as mayor. It is suspected that this was a deliberate rumor spread by traitors to disrupt the political situation. It is currently under investigation. The city's public security is absolutely responsible, and the illegal plots of certain people have not had a chance to riot due to close surveillance and have gradually become a thing of the past. (15th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) After Tianjin Mayor Xiao Zhenying submitted his resignation, the deadlock regarding the selection of a successor has not yet been broken. It is now known that Song Zheyuan's 29th Army is still supporting Xiao's retention; otherwise, they must select someone from the army to succeed him and are strongly opposed to Qi Xieyuan as his successor. (15th Reuters Dispatch)

Sugiyama Flew to Zhangjiakou Yesterday

(Beiping) Sugiyama, the Vice Chief of Staff, arrived in Beiping from Tianjin on the 13th and met with Song Zheyuan. This morning, he flew to Zhangjiakou on a Japanese military plane with his entourage for inspection. Matsumuro and Kawabe, the commander of the brigade stationed in Beiping of the North China Garrison, went to the airport to see them off. Sugiyama is scheduled to fly back to Beiping tomorrow. (15th Special Dispatch)

Chiang Banqueted Wang Chonghui Yesterday

(Nanjing) After arriving in Nanjing, Wang Chonghui has been busy visiting various friends. He rested at his residence on the morning of the 15th and met with Li Liejun and many former colleagues in the judicial field. At 1 PM, President Chiang hosted a banquet for Wang at his residence, inviting the heads of various Yuan, Ministries, and Committees to accompany him. After the banquet, Wang returned to his residence to rest. Sun Ke visited, and Deng Jiayan hosted a banquet in the evening. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Central Government Holds Two Memorial Weeks

Sun Ke Presides and Reports at the Central Government; Chairman Lin of the National Government Speaks on National Spirit

(Nanjing) The Central Government held the 28th Memorial Week at 9 AM on the 15th. Vice Chairman Chiang and Central Committee members Lin Sen, Sun Ke, Chen Lifu, He Yingqin, Cheng Qian, Chen Shaokuan, Jiang Zuobin, Gan Naiguang, Li Wenfan, Zhou Qigang, Fang Zhi, Shao Yuanchong, Miao Peicheng, Xu Enzeng, Chen Ce, Wang Luyi, Chu Minyi, Huang Musong, Zhu Peide, Luo Jialun, Qian Dajun, Shao Hua, Hong Lanyou, and Chen Shuren, as well as all staff members, totaling approximately 700 people, attended. Chairman Sun Ke led the ceremony and then gave a speech. The ceremony concluded at 9:45 AM. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The National Government held Memorial Week at 10 AM on the 15th. Sun Li, Niu Yongjian, Deng Jiayan, Wang Boqun, Huang Fusheng, Cheng Qian, Chen Shaokuan, Chen Shuren, Chen Xunyong, Chen Qicai, Lu Chao, Wei Huai, and other officials from the National Government and various Yuan, Ministries, and Committees, totaling approximately 500 people, attended. Chairman Lin led the ceremony and gave a speech on "National Spirit and National Survival," which concluded at 10:30 AM. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Chairman Lin gave a speech on "National Spirit and National Survival" at the National Government's Memorial Week on the morning of the 15th. First, based on the Premier's will, he explained the theme in great detail. Second, he explained the importance of national spirit to national survival and cited various examples to prove the unchanging truth that "a nation must maintain its national spirit in order to survive in the world." Third, he stated that national spirit is a kind of national self-confidence, that is, a belief that the constituent members of a nation have in their own nation. With this belief, the nation can be united and exert great strength. Using this strength, the nation can actively seek its own survival and development, and passively resist the oppression of foreign nations. This is a kind of national spirit. In short, national spirit is the driving force for national survival. To cultivate national spirit, one must know the various advantages of one's own nation in terms of history and culture, so as to arouse faith in one's own nation and create strong national self-confidence. As a result, this nation can naturally survive forever in the world. Finally, he said that the root cause of our country's weakness is that our national spirit has declined and we have lost our national self-confidence. Now, to rescue our nation from its oppressed position, this erroneous mentality must be corrected as soon as possible. The method of correction is to know that we originally had good habits and that our knowledge and abilities are no weaker than those of others. We must have this belief in our own nation in order to revitalize the national spirit and strive for the nation's survival and development. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Hong Kong Implements Anti-Gas Training

(Hong Kong) Hong Kong is implementing anti-gas training, starting with the ambulance team, and is increasing the production of 500,000 gas masks to meet needs. (15th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Standardizes Titles in Diplomatic Notes

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has standardized the titles in diplomatic notes. The original titles (His Excellency the Ambassador Extraordinary and Plenipotentiary of [Country Name] to China) and the character "Da" (Great) in (Great Republic of China, date) will be temporarily removed from all diplomatic notes from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to the embassies of various countries in China. Further regulations will be made after future conferences determine the format of the titles. (15th Special Dispatch)

Chen Lu Visits Chairman Lin

Current Commentary

The Issue of Lifting Sanctions Against Italy

— Lang

Since Italy announced the annexation of the entire Abyssinia last month, the League of Nations has encountered an unprecedented crisis. This crisis is whether the League of Nations will tacitly accept the facts created by Italy's use of force or prevent them. If it is recognized, it will be tantamount to slapping oneself in the face. If economic sanctions against Italy continue to be maintained, they will not be allowed by the facts. At this crossroads, the League of Nations has fallen into a very depressed state. Now, the special meeting of the Council of the League of Nations and the special conference of the League of Nations convened at the proposal of Argentina have been scheduled to be held at the end of the month. The issue of sanctions against Italy cannot but be resolved.

How will the League of Nations resolve the unprecedented crisis it has encountered? In other words, is the League of Nations prepared to intensify sanctions against Italy or lift economic sanctions? To explain this issue, it is necessary to first examine the attitude of the British government, because the League of Nations' implementation of economic sanctions against Italy can largely be said to have been initiated by the British. Since Italy announced the annexation of Abyssinia, the British government, with the exception of a few cabinet members, has been in favor of lifting economic sanctions, but it has not dared to make a clear decision due to the strong force of public opinion. Now, due to the development of the situation, the faction in the government that favors lifting sanctions has clearly taken the upper hand. This can be seen from the following facts: Former Foreign Secretary Hoare's return to the cabinet as First Lord of the Admiralty. Hoare is a well-known pro-Italian. Last year, he drafted a peace proposal with French Prime Minister Laval to partition Abyssinia, but he stepped down after being attacked by public opinion. It is said that the condition for Hoare's return to the cabinet this time is to withdraw the British fleet from the Mediterranean. In a public speech on June 10, Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain advocated lifting economic sanctions against Italy. Chamberlain is an important figure in the cabinet and is likely to succeed Baldwin as prime minister. His words can naturally represent the majority opinion of the government. In addition, there are quite a few government officials who advocate lifting economic sanctions. Now, not only does Britain intend to end sanctions against Italy, but other member states such as Chile, Argentina, and Czechoslovakia also have the same tendency. Therefore, it can now be said that the League of Nations conference to be held at the end of this month will largely decide to lift sanctions against Italy.

The fundamental reason for the League of Nations' intention to lift sanctions against Italy is due to the selfishness and self-interest of the imperialists, who are unwilling to uphold the interests of small and weak nations. However, Italy's serious threat is also an important reason. Italian Ambassador to Britain Grandi visited British Undersecretary of State for Foreign Affairs on June 9 and said that the implementation of economic sanctions by the League of Nations was intended to curb the Italian-Abyssinian war, but now that the war has ended, the sanctions have lost their purpose. If the League of Nations still decides to maintain economic sanctions at the end of this month, Italy will definitely announce its withdrawal from the League of Nations, which is something that Britain and France are extremely unwilling to see. At the same time, Italy is preparing to mobilize 800,000 troops and promote the conclusion of a military alliance with Germany and other means to threaten Britain and France to lift economic sanctions against Italy.

But will the League of Nations completely and unconditionally succumb to Italy's serious threat? This will not happen, because Britain also wants to save face. The tragicomedy that is scheduled to be played out in Geneva now is that on the one hand, the implementation of sanctions against Italy will be lifted, and on the other hand, it will still be decided not to recognize the legality of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia. At the same time, it is also preparing to amend the Covenant of the League of Nations to avoid the recurrence of the same facts in the future. Such a trick is of course not welcomed by our peace-loving people. The British League of Nations Union has already held a meeting on the 14th to oppose the lifting of economic sanctions against Italy. British Labor Party leader Attlee also issued a similar statement of opposition. We can only wait for the facts to tell us how the situation will evolve in the future.

Japanese Military Plans to Strengthen Air Force to Counter Russia; Discuss Setting Up Special Department to Develop Civil Aviation; Exaggerated Propaganda of Soviet Military Expansion

(Tokyo) The idea that civil aviation is the second army of the air force in the event of war is a thing of the past. The Soviet Union is actively preparing to realize this plan, with civil aviation itself as the air force. It is reported that the national air force mobilization project has accommodated 18 million people last year, and 9% of the soldiers in the country are reservists who have completed air force education. There are about 70 aircraft manufacturing factories, with an annual manufacturing capacity of no less than 2,500 aircraft. The Japanese Ministry of the Army believes that with such developed Soviet aviation, it is absolutely impossible to win a modern war even with all efforts to strengthen the army and navy air corps. It is determined to actively strengthen national defense and expand civil aviation. After various studies, it has reached the conclusion to establish a large organization such as an aviation ministry or an aviation institute to actively assist the development of civil aviation. It is currently in consultation with the naval authorities. After obtaining the navy's consent, it will jointly submit a request to the cabinet for approval. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

Next Year's Army and Navy Budget to Exceed 1.4 Billion Yuan

(Tokyo) The government ministries are currently drafting next year's budget proposal based on the resolutions and recommendations of the temporary parliament, preparing to submit it to the cabinet meeting on July 3 for review. Those who pay attention to the current situation are extremely concerned about the national defense budgets of the army and navy. It is reported that the army, in view of the current international situation, has proposed a comprehensive national defense policy, so next year's national defense budget will reach as much as 700 million yuan, attempting to complete the strengthened national defense in the next four or six years. The first step is to increase the military strength in "Manchuria", enrich aviation and air defense equipment, and strengthen the ability to fight against Russia. As for the navy, the main focus is to build battleships, improve aviation power, expand naval and land forces, and carry out a southward policy. Its budget must also exceed 700 million yuan. (China United Press dispatch on the 15th)

(Tokyo) According to reports from the Tokyo Asahi and Yomiuri newspapers, the Soviet Union has recently continued its acts of aggression. The Japanese army should increase its combat power, with North Manchuria as the first line of national defense. After maintaining equal strength with Russia, it should establish a demilitarized zone and demand that the Soviet Union withdraw its troops. The two newspapers also published the army's views on this issue as follows:

The army authorities are convinced that the best way to make the Soviet Union abandon its provocative behavior is to strengthen Japanese military equipment. They are now actively preparing military power. A 50-kilometer demilitarized zone should be established on the Russian-Manchurian border, and the Japanese-Manchurian army and the Soviet army should withdraw their troops from the zone.

The Soviet Union claims a non-aggression treaty, but on the one hand, it is building fortresses on the border and assembling troops. Japan knows that the true intentions of the Soviet Union cannot be assured by this treaty. If a demilitarized zone is established, all kinds of pending issues between Japan, Manchuria, and the Soviet Union can be easily resolved.

The most important thing in the Soviet Union's Far East policy is to obtain an ice-free military port in the Far East, and to use the communization of the Far East as the basis for communizing the world.

The Japanese army will not move a single soldier without the order of the Emperor, so there is no such thing as the Japanese army challenging. The army should strengthen its national defense in preparation for unforeseen events. The army should adjust the Russian-Manchurian relationship with a strong military background, so it is easy to resolve border incidents. (Domei dispatch on the 15th)

(London) It is almost certain that the British government will take action on the issue of lifting sanctions against Italy. The diplomatic reporter for the Morning Post claimed that "When the British cabinet meets this Wednesday, it will definitely take a definite decision on the following two issues: lifting sanctions against Italy and reorganizing the League of Nations and reducing its current powers." However, it is very doubtful whether Foreign Secretary Eden can continue to serve after these two measures are decided. The diplomatic reporter for the Manchester Guardian expressed the same view, but clearly adopted a reserved attitude, saying, "The British government's attitude should be regarded as not formally decided until the cabinet meeting is held on Wednesday. As for the extraordinary meeting of the Council of the League of Nations to be held on the 26th of this month, if all countries are unwilling to make recommendations on the issue of lifting sanctions against Italy, then the British representative should propose ending the sanctions or organizing a committee to re-examine the sanctions issue. This is more credible." In addition, regarding the reorganization of the League of Nations, the newspaper also published a commentary, believing that this should be based on the following two principles: regional organization of security agencies, and the conclusion of a Mediterranean Convention, with Italy in a leading position. It also said that there are no terms of exchange between lifting sanctions and Italy's participation in the Mediterranean Convention. Finally, the newspaper also considered it inaccurate that the original position of the United Kingdom in the Mediterranean had been weakened, but said that the United Kingdom might reorganize its original position, and the situation on Malta is no longer what it used to be. It may be necessary to establish another naval base in another area that is not easily attacked by the enemy, for example, to replace it. In addition, a naval base should be added to Cape Town in the South African Federation as a new route to India. (Havas dispatch on the 15th)

Hitler Seeks Opportunity to Demand Recovery of Former Colonies

Before British-Italian Relations are Clear, He Does Not Want to Announce Policy Prematurely

(Berlin) It was learned today that Chancellor Hitler is now seeking an opportunity to demand the recovery of the former German colonies. Although the United Kingdom is currently exerting pressure, demanding that Germany explain its policies, Hitler will not reply prematurely before thoroughly studying the various issues. Hitler is currently paying the most attention to the following points: the competition between Britain and Italy for hegemony in the Mediterranean, the relationship between Britain and Italy, and the staff meeting of the Little Entente countries held in Bucharest. Therefore, Hitler does not want to announce his policy before British-Italian relations are completely clear so that he can decide which country to be close to. Hitler told Italian Prime Minister Mussolini that he was against the restoration of the Austrian Habsburg dynasty. (National Press dispatch on the 14th)

Success of the French Peaceful Revolution; People's Front Rallies and Demonstrates; Celebrating the Victory of the Labor Movement

The Labor Strikes of the Past Two Weeks Have Generally Come to an End; The Machines in the Factories are Hummin Classed Picturesque Re-Emitting Thick Smoke

(Paris) The various parties of the leftist People's Front held demonstrations in all major cities throughout the country today to celebrate the election victory. There were thousands of people marching in formation on the streets everywhere, led by the French tricolor national flag and the Third International red flag. The situation was good and no accidents occurred. It is scheduled to be held again on July 14, which is French National Day. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

(Paris) This strike movement was launched by the Lavallette Electrical Metallurgical Factory in Saint-Ouen, a suburb of Paris, on May 27. Afterwards, the various factories in the metallurgical industry followed suit, extending to other industries, and evolved into a huge labor strike. By 7:30 AM to 8:30 AM this morning, the major metallurgical factories in the capital area and the Seine province had resumed work one after another. The chimneys were again seen spraying thick smoke, and the sound of machines in the factories was again heard. All technicians and workers had returned to their posts, and the employees in the office were also working at their desks. After the end of the metallurgical industry strike movement, it is no exaggeration to infer that the huge labor strike that has lasted for half a month will come to a complete end. The strike movements in other industries such as construction, ceramics, pharmaceuticals, electricity, and hairdressing have also come to an end. However, workers in the shipping industry, department stores, insurance, clothing, and perfume industries, as well as funeral home employees and jockeys at racetracks, have not yet signed agreements with the capitalists, but the end is not far off. As for several small factories in the metallurgical industry, they have not yet resumed work because the wage issues are still to be adjusted and resolved. It is expected that an agreement will be reached today and a satisfactory solution will be obtained. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

The middle class can rest assured," and so on. This is what we desire, and this is what the Communist Party should do," and so on. At 8:00 PM, the meeting was adjourned. The proceedings of the day were smooth and no incidents occurred. China's Industrial Decline: Unequal Treaties Are the Culprit; Smuggling in North China Causes Significant Losses; China's Labor Representatives Speak with Pain

(Geneva) During the debate at the International Labor Bureau Conference today, China's labor representative, Mr. Zhu, stated that the decline of Chinese industry is due to frequent natural disasters internally and the constraints of unequal treaties and imperialist aggression externally. Zhu also criticized the imperialists in the capitalist world. He then asked the public to pay attention to the frequent occurrence of factory disasters, especially in the Shanghai Public Concession. The severe state of the recession is caused by the dumping of foreign goods, which damages the sales market of domestic products. Smuggling in North China, in the nine months up to April 1, is estimated to have caused China losses of 25.5 million yuan. The situation of 10 million overseas Chinese compatriots is even worse than that of domestic labor compatriots. The International Labor Bureau should investigate the conditions for recruiting Chinese workers, and the Board of Directors should travel to the Far East to strengthen the relationship between China and the International Labor Bureau. Zhu supported the proposal to convene an Asian Labor Conference. (Reuters dispatch on the 15th)

(Geneva) Zhu Xuefan, the labor representative of China at the International Labor Conference, talked about the fact that China is undoubtedly extremely backward in production. Now that all countries in the world are striving for economic recovery, China is still shrouded in recession. Goods imported from various countries into China have penetrated into the interior, and even small villages have been invaded by foreign goods, which has greatly impacted China's handicraft industry. In the past nine months of smuggling in North China, customs losses reached 25.5 million yuan. As a result, not only is China's small industry, which is in its infancy, being destroyed, but also the legitimate trade of various countries is being undermined. Domestic and international markets are suffering losses. Capitalists, relying on unequal treaties, exploit the low wages of Chinese workers and enjoy various conveniences, while the lives of workers are greatly affected due to economic depression. Especially in the concessions, factory inspections are impossible, making their lives even more dangerous. It is hoped that the conference can provide relief, and it is hoped that the authorities of the Labor Bureau can conduct on-the-spot investigations in the Far East to obtain more opportunities for contact. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 15th)

Inauguration of the New Building of the Chinese Academy in Frankfurt, Germany

Ambassador Cheng Presides Over the Opening Ceremony

Special Arrangement of Museum Exhibits

Sufficient to Represent Modern Chinese Life

Frankfurt: The new site of the Chinese Academy here was inaugurated today by Ambassador Cheng. A large number of prominent figures gathered at the ceremony, including Chinese students from the University of Frankfurt, the mayor of the city, and other prominent figures from the art, science, and industrial communities. The chairman, former German Minister to China and current President of the Academy, Mr. Boekger, delivered a speech, welcoming the guests and thanking the German government for its assistance, which enabled the Academy to achieve such success. Ambassador Cheng Tianfang and Ambassador Doddmann then delivered speeches, both stating that the mission of the new location should be to increase friendship between the two countries. Afterwards, the guests visited the museum to view the antique exhibits.

The Chinese Academy was founded in 1925 by the famous scholar Mr. Wilhelm. Since Mr. Wilhelm's death, its scope has expanded daily. All kinds of Chinese art have been gradually collected, making it now a very magnificent museum. However, the Academy is not named as a museum because its purpose is not to display Chinese antiques, but to represent "modern Chinese life." From this perspective, this type of exhibition is rare. The antiquities collected here are sufficient to represent ancient Chinese art and cultural life. There are many types of exhibits, but each item is exactly the same as it is used in China today. Among them are family sacrificial items, furniture, and utensils, arranged in the same way as Chinese family decorations, which is completely different from the display method of ordinary museums. In addition, there is also a Chinese-style study, bedroom, and living room, the stage set of Chinese drama, and all kinds of ancient costumes, etc. The second floor is a Chinese library with 12,000 Chinese books and 2,500 books about China. This kind of display is very eye-catching to Europeans, and the impression of China on the visitors is also very good. (National Telegram, 14th)

Full Text of the Draft Soviet Constitution (Part Two)

Chapter Four: Supreme Governing Bodies of the Federal Republics

Article 57: The highest governing body of each federal republic is the Supreme Soviet (Verkhovnyi Soviet) of that federal republic.

Article 58: The Supreme Soviet of each federal republic shall be elected by the citizens of that republic for a term of four years. The ratio of representatives shall be determined by the constitution of each federal republic.

Article 59: The Supreme Soviet of each federal republic is the sole legislative body of that republic.

Article 60: The powers of the Supreme Soviet of each federal republic are:

A. To enact and amend the constitution of the republic, in accordance with Article 16 of the Soviet Constitution;

B. To approve the laws of the autonomous republics within its jurisdiction and to define their territories;

C. To approve the national economic plans and budgets of the republic;

D. To exercise the power of amnesty and pardon for citizens sentenced by the judicial organs of the republic.

Article 61: The Supreme Soviet of each federal republic shall elect a chairman of the Supreme Soviet, including one chairman of the Presidium, several vice-chairmen, and several members of the Presidium. The powers of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of each federal republic shall be defined by the laws of that republic.

Article 62: The Supreme Soviet of each federal republic shall elect a chairman and several vice-chairmen to guide the meetings.

Article 63: The Supreme Soviet of each federal republic shall organize the government of that republic – the Council of People's Commissars of the federal republic.

Chapter Five: State Administrative Organs of the Soviet Union

Article 64: The highest executive and administrative organ of state power of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics is the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union.

Article 65: The Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union is responsible to the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union. Article 66: The Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union may issue resolutions, orders, and regulations in accordance with and for the implementation of current laws and to supervise their implementation.

Article 67: The orders and regulations of the Council of People's Commissars shall have mandatory power and shall be universally implemented throughout the territory of the Soviet Union.

Article 68: The powers of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union are:

A. To unify and guide the work of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, the United People's Commissariats, and other economic and cultural organs;

B. To devise methods to implement the national economic plan and the state budget, and to consolidate the credit of the monetary system;

C. To devise methods to maintain public order, protect national interests, and safeguard the rights of citizens;

D. To maintain the general direction of foreign state relations;

E. To determine the annual conscription quota for citizens liable for military service and to guide the establishment of national armed forces.

Article 69: The Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union has the right to suspend the regulations and orders of the Councils of People's Commissars of the federal republics and to cancel the orders and instructions of the People's Commissariats of the Soviet Union in the administrative and economic departments within the scope of the Soviet Union’s authority.

Article 70: The Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union is organized by the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union and includes the following members: the Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, the Vice-Chairmen of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, the Chairman of the State Planning Committee of the Soviet Union, the Chairman of the Administration Committee of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, the Chairman of the Agricultural Procurement Committee, the Chairman of the Arts Committee, and the Chairman of the Higher Education Committee.

Article 71: The Soviet government or a Soviet People's Commissar must provide an oral or written response to the questions of the representatives of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union within three days in the Chamber.

Article 72: The People's Commissars of the Soviet Union are responsible for managing the affairs of the national administrative departments within the scope of the Soviet Union's authority.

Article 73: Within the scope of their respective powers, the People's Commissars of the Soviet Union may issue orders and instructions in accordance with and for the implementation of existing laws, as well as the regulations and orders of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, and to supervise their implementation.

Article 74: The People's Commissars of the Soviet Union are divided into two types: Federal People's Commissars and Federal-Republican People's Commissars (United People's Commissars).

Article 75: The Federal People's Commissars manage the affairs of the national administrative departments for which they are responsible directly or through their appointed organs throughout the Soviet Union.

Article 76: The United People's Commissars manage the affairs of the national administrative departments for which they are responsible through the People's Commissars of the same name in the federal republics.

Article 77: The following People's Commissariats are all Federal People's Commissariats: National Defense, Foreign Affairs, Foreign Trade, Transportation, Communications, Water Transport, and Heavy Industry.

Article 78: The following People's Commissariats are all United People's Commissariats: Food industry, Light industry, Timber industry, Agriculture, State grain and livestock farms, Finance, Domestic trade, Internal affair, Judiciary, and Health.

Chapter Six: State Administrative Organs of the Federal Republics

Article 79: The highest executive and administrative organ of state power of the federal republics is the Council of People's Commissars of the federal republics.

Article 80: The Council of People's Commissars of the federal republics is responsible to the Supreme Soviet of that republic.

Article 81: The federal republics may issue regulations and orders in accordance with and for the implementation of the laws of the Soviet Union and that republic, as well as the regulations and orders of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, and to supervise their implementation.

Article 82: The Council of People's Commissars of the federal republics has the right to suspend the regulations and orders of the Councils of People's Commissars of the autonomous republics and to cancel the resolutions and orders of the Executive Committees of the Soviets of Workers' Deputies of the districts, provinces, and autonomous provinces.

Article 83: The Council of People's Commissars of the federal republics is organized by the Supreme Soviet of that republic and includes the following members: the Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars of the republic, the Vice-Chairmen of the Council of People's Commissars of the republic, the Chairman of the State Planning Committee, the People's Commissars for Food Industry, Light Industry, Timber Industry, Agriculture, State Grain and Livestock Farms, Finance, Domestic Trade , Interior, Justice, Health, Education, Local Industry, Urban Economy, Insurance, Chairman of the People's Commissariat for Agricultural Procurement, Minister of Art, and representatives of the Federal People's Commissariats.

Article 84: The People's Commissars of the federal republics manage the affairs of the national administrative departments within the scope of authority of that republic.

Article 85: Within the scope of their respective powers, the People's Commissars of the federal republics may issue orders and instructions in accordance with and for the implementation of the laws of the Soviet Union and that republic, the orders and regulations of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union and that republic, and the orders and instructions of the United People's Commissariats of the Soviet Union.

Article 86: The People's Commissars of the federal republics are divided into two types: United People's Commissars and Republican People's Commissars.

Article 87: The United People's Commissars manage the affairs of the national administrative departments for which they are responsible, and are responsible to both the Council of People's Commissars of that republic and the respective United People's Commissars of the Soviet Union.

Article 88: The Republican People's Commissars manage the affairs of the national administrative departments for which they are responsible, and are directly responsible to the Council of People's Commissars of that republic.

Chapter Seven: Highest Organs of State Power of Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republics

Article 89: The highest organ of state power of an autonomous Soviet socialist republic is the Supreme Soviet of the autonomous Soviet socialist republic.

Article 90: The Supreme Soviet of an autonomous republic shall be elected by the citizens of that republic for a term of four years. The ratio of representatives shall be determined by the constitution of that autonomous republic.

Article 91: The Supreme Soviet of an autonomous republic is the sole legislative body of that autonomous Soviet socialist republic.

Article 92: Each autonomous republic shall formulate its own constitution, explaining the special form of the autonomous republic, and it must not conflict with the constitution of the federal republic directly under the federation.

Article 93: According to the constitution of the autonomous republic, the autonomous republic shall elect the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet and organize the Council of People's Commissars of the autonomous republic.

Chapter Eight: Local Organs of State Power

Article 94: The organs of state power in districts, provinces, autonomous provinces, counties (okrugs, rayons), cities, and villages (including stanitsas, khutors, kishlaks, auls) are the Soviets of Workers' Deputies (Soviets).

Article 95: The Soviets of Workers' Deputies of each district, province, autonomous province, county, city, and village shall be elected by the workers of that district, province, autonomous province, county, city, and village for a term of two years.

Article 96: The ratio of election of the Soviets of Workers' Deputies shall be determined by the constitution of each federal republic.

Article 97: The Soviets of Workers' Deputies shall guide the various activities of the subordinate administrative organs, protect the rights of citizens, carry out local economic and cultural construction, and formulate local budgets.

Article 98: Within the powers granted to them by the laws of the Soviet Union and the federal republics directly under the federation, the Soviets of Workers' Deputies may formulate resolutions and issue instructions.

Article 99: The executive and administrative organs of the Soviets of Workers' Deputies of each district, province, autonomous province, county, city, and village are their executive committees. The executive committees are elected by the Soviets of Workers' Deputies and include a chairman, a vice-chairman, and several members.

Article 100: According to the constitution of each federal republic, the executive and administrative organs of the Soviets of Workers' Deputies of small villages may be presided over by the chairman and several vice-chairmen elected by the Soviets of Workers' Deputies.

Article 101: The executive organs of the Soviets of Workers' Deputies are directly responsible to both the Soviets of Workers' Deputies and the executive organs of the higher-level Soviets of Workers' Deputies.

Chapter Nine: Courts and Prosecutorial Organs

Article 102: The judicial power of the Soviet Union is exercised by the Supreme Court of the Soviet Union, the Supreme Courts of the federal republics, the district courts, the provincial courts, the courts of the autonomous republics and autonomous provinces, the special courts of the Soviet Union (which are organized by the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union), and the People's Courts.

Article 103: Unless otherwise specified by law, all levels of courts must have people's assessors participating in the trial.

Article 104: The Supreme Court of the Soviet Union is the highest judicial organ, and it has the power to supervise the activities of all levels of courts in the Soviet Union and the federal republics.

Article 105: The Supreme Court of the Soviet Union and the Special Courts of the Soviet Union are elected by the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union for a term of five years.

Article 106: The Supreme Courts of the federal republics are elected by the Supreme Soviets of those republics for a term of five years.

Article 107: The Supreme Courts of the autonomous republics are elected by the Supreme Soviets of those autonomous republics for a term of five years.

Article 108: The district courts, provincial courts, and courts of the autonomous provinces are elected by the Soviets of Workers' Deputies of those districts, provinces, and autonomous provinces for a term of five years.

Article 109: The People's Courts are elected by the citizens of each county through a universal, direct, and equal voting system for a term of three years.

Article 110: Court trials shall be conducted in the language of the federal or autonomous republic or autonomous province. If the person on trial does not know these languages, a translator must be used to ensure that he fully understands the contents of the case and has the right to present to the court in his dialect.

Article 111: Unless otherwise provided by law and the accused is granted the right to defense and guaranteed, all levels of courts in the Soviet Union must conduct open trials.

Article 112: Judges are independent and are restricted only by law.

Article 113: The highest supervisory power over whether the People's Commissars and their subordinate organs, as well as civil servants and citizens of the Soviet Union, comply with the law belongs to the Prosecutor of the Soviet Union.

Article 114: The Prosecutor of the Soviet Union is elected by the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union for a term of seven years.

Article 115: The prosecutors of each republic, district, and province, as well as the prosecutors of each autonomous republic and autonomous province, are appointed by the Prosecutor of the Soviet Union for a term of five years.

Article 116: The county prosecutors are appointed by the federal People's Republic prosecutors, subject to the approval of the Prosecutor of the Soviet Union, for a term of five years.

Article 117: All levels of prosecutorial organs may independently exercise their powers and are responsible only to the Supreme Prosecutor of the Soviet Union.

Chapter Ten: Fundamental Rights and Obligations of Citizens

Article 118: Citizens of the Soviet Union have the right to work – the right to guaranteed employment and remuneration in accordance with the amount and nature of their work. The right to work is guaranteed by the following facts: the socialist organization of the national economy and the continued development of Soviet social productive forces due to the elimination of economic panic and the elimination of unemployment.

Article 119: Citizens of the Soviet Union have the right to rest, and rest is guaranteed by the following facts: the reduction of working hours to seven hours for the vast majority of workers, annual vacations for employees, and continued payment of wages, as well as the establishment of a vast network of sanatoriums, rest homes, and clubs for workers.

Article 120: Citizens of the Soviet Union have the right to social security in old age, sickness, or loss of working capacity. This right is guaranteed by the following facts: the extensive development of worker social insurance at state expense, free medical care, and the establishment of a vast network for the protection of the health of workers.

Article 121: Citizens of the Soviet Union have the right to education. This right is guaranteed by the following facts: the universality of free and compulsory basic education, even up to higher education, state subsidies for the vast majority of students in higher education institutions, the teaching of local languages in all schools, and the free industrial, technical, and agricultural education organizations for workers in factories, state farms, machine tractor stations, and collective farms.

Article 122: Women in the Soviet Union enjoy equal rights with men in political, economic, cultural, and social life. The realization of these rights of women is made possible by the following facts: women enjoy equal rights with men in work, remuneration, rest, social insurance, and education, the state protects the interests of motherhood and childhood, gives pregnant women leave and pays wages, and establishes a vast network of maternity homes, nurseries, and kindergartens.

Article 123: Citizens of the Soviet Union, regardless of their nationality or ethnicity, enjoy equal rights in political, economic, cultural, and social life. This is an immutable law. Any direct or indirect restriction of these rights, or the granting of certain privileges to a portion of citizens based on ethnic or national distinction, as well as any propaganda of racial or national exclusion, hatred, and contempt, is punishable by law.

Article 125: In accordance with the interests of the workers and to consolidate the socialist system, citizens of the Soviet Union enjoy the following rights: A. Freedom of speech, B. Freedom of publication, C. Freedom of assembly, D. Freedom of street parades and demonstrations. These civil rights are guaranteed by the following facts: the establishment of printing houses, the supply of paper, public housing, streets, transportation, and other necessary material resources for the use of the workers and their organizations.

Article 126: In accordance with the interests of the workers and to develop the independent organization and political activities of the masses, the people of the Soviet Union have the right to organize public organs, such as trade unions, cooperatives, youth groups, sports and national defense groups, and cultural, technical, and scientific groups, and to organize the most active and conscious citizens of the working class and other working strata into the Communist Party of the Soviet Union, which is the vanguard of the workers' efforts to consolidate and develop the socialist system, and represents the leadership center of the various organizations of the people and the state laborers.

Article 127: The person of citizens of the Soviet Union is inviolable. No citizen may be arrested except by court order or with the consent of the prosecutor.

Article 128: The home of citizens is inviolable, and the secrecy of their correspondence is protected by law.

Article 129: The Soviet Union grants the right of asylum to foreign citizens who are persecuted for protecting the interests of the workers, or for their scientific activities, or for struggling for national liberation.

Article 130: Any citizen of the Soviet Union has the obligation to obey the Constitution of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics, abide by the law, enforce labor discipline, faithfully fulfill social obligations, and abide by the rules of socialist public life.

Article 131: Any citizen of the Soviet Union has the obligation to protect and consolidate public socialist property, regard it as the sacred and inviolable foundation of the Soviet system, regard it as the source of wealth and power of their motherland, and regard it as the source of prosperity and civilized life for all workers. Anyone who attempts to infringe on public and socialist property is an enemy of the people.

Article 132: Citizens have the obligation to serve in the military. Military service in the Workers' and Peasants' Red Army is an honorable obligation of citizens of the Soviet Union.

Article 133: Defending the motherland is the sacred obligation of every citizen of the Soviet Union. Traitors of the motherland, violating oaths, surrendering to the enemy, harming the country's military strength, and acting as foreign spies are the greatest sins and are subject to the most severe penalties under the law.

Chapter Eleven: Electoral System

Article 134: The representatives of the Soviets of Workers' Deputies at all levels (Soviets), namely the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, the Supreme Soviets of the federal republics, the Soviets of Workers' Deputies of each province and district, the Supreme Soviets of the autonomous republics, and the representatives of the Soviets of Workers' Deputies of each autonomous province, county, city, and village, shall be elected by the voters through a universal, equal, direct, and secret ballot system.

Article 135: Elections for representatives are conducted on a universal system. Any citizen of the Soviet Union who has reached the age of eighteen in the election year has the right to vote and be elected, with the exception of those with mental defects and those who have been deprived of the right to vote by the court.

Article 136: Elections for representatives are conducted on an equal system. Any citizen has equal rights to vote and be elected, regardless of race, ethnicity, religious belief, education level, place of residence, social status, property status, and past activities.

Article 137: Women have the right to vote and be elected, under the same conditions as men.

Article 138: Citizens serving in the Red Army have the right to vote and be elected, under the same conditions as all citizens.

Article 139: Elections for representatives are conducted on a direct system. Elections for all levels of Soviets of Workers' Deputies, from the Soviets of Workers' Deputies of villages and cities to the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, are conducted by direct voting by citizens.

Article 140: Elections for representatives are conducted on a secret system.

Article 141: Candidates for election are proposed by regions. Various social groups of workers, the Communist Party, trade unions, cooperatives, youth groups, and cultural groups have the right to propose candidates.

Article 142: Any representative must report his work and the work of the Soviet of Workers' Deputies to the voters, and at any time, he may be recalled by a resolution of the majority of the voters in accordance with legal procedures.

Article 143: The national emblem of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics is a globe illuminated by sunlight, decorated with a hammer and sickle, surrounded by ears of grain, and inscribed in the languages of the federal republics, "Workers of all countries, unite!" The above national emblem also has a five-pointed red star, surrounded by a gold border.

Article 144: The national flag of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics is a red flag, with a gold hammer and sickle in the upper corner near the flagpole, above which is a five-pointed red star surrounded by a gold border. The ratio of length to width is one to two.

Article 145: The capital of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics is the city of Moscow.

Chapter Thirteen: Amendments to the Constitution

Article 146: Amendments to the Soviet Constitution require a resolution passed by a majority of two-thirds or more of both chambers of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union.

Correction: "Chapter Three: The Supreme State Power Organs of the Soviet Union" should be placed before Article 30.
