High Court Dismissed Clerk Zhu Xiongwu and Others Accused of Fraud and Extortion

Chen Chaozuan Granted Bail of 500 Yuan, Zhu Lu Remanded in Custody, Case to be Heard Again Next Monday

Zhu Xiongwu and Chen Chaozuan, dismissed clerks from the Jiangsu High Court, were previously discovered to have colluded with Lu Wenguang, who acted as a lawyer's clerk, to defraud litigants and extort money. The Wuxian District Court investigated and confirmed these facts, and filed a public prosecution. The Supreme Court ruled that the case should be transferred to the Shanghai First Special District Court for trial. Judge Huang Risheng previously conducted a preliminary hearing, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, the court resumed the hearing. More than ten witnesses were summoned, but several failed to appear. Judge Huang first examined Lu Wenguang regarding the charges in the indictment, specifically the handling of Li Shannan's appeal. Witness Li Shannan testified that he was friends with Lu Wenguang. He stated that he had previously been sentenced to one year in prison and fined 1,000 yuan by the Shanghai District Court for fraud. Last April, he appealed to the Jiangsu High Court, and his wife asked Lu to draft the appeal. Lu predicted that the sentence could be reduced by six months, but the result was only the cancellation of the fine, while the prison sentence remained one year. Therefore, he later wrote to Lu, stating his inability to pay the promised reward of 200 yuan. When questioned, Lu Wenguang stated that the reduction of six months was merely a hope he expressed to Li's wife, not a guarantee. Next, Zhu Xiongwu was examined regarding the inquiry into the proceedings of the Chen Yuzhang inheritance case. According to Ma Runde, a clerk from the Jiangsu High Court, Shen, the judge, handled the case of the inheritance retrial for Chen Yuzhang, et al. Zhu Xiongwu inquired about the progress of the case with me in September of last year. I told him that they were currently being asked to pay the litigation fees. I did not notice whether Zhu looked through the case file at the time. When questioned, Zhu denied this entirely. Next, the Shanghai Yutai Firm and the Wuxi Zou Chengtai Rice Mill were questioned regarding Zhu Xiongwu's participation in the mediation of a debt dispute. According to Jiang Hongbin, a partner in the Yutai Firm, he invited Xu Hongchang and Ji Yunxiang to go to Wuxi to collect the debt owed by Zou Chengtai. On the evening of September 2nd last year, a settlement was reached between the two parties at Ji Yunxiang's home in Wuxi. Yang Shaoyun, the owner of the Xin Wuxi Newspaper, also participated. At that time, Zou Chengtai repaid 5,000 yuan of the debt. I took out 2,000 yuan and gave it to Xu Hongchang, instructing him to give it to Ji Yunqing and Yang Shaoyun as a reward for their efforts. Zhu Xiongwu was not present. When Judge Zhang of the Jiangsu High Court came to investigate on January 16th this year, I did not say that I was introduced to Zhu in Wuxi. As for the missing 7,000 yuan from the store's accounts, it was due to years of embezzlement by the manager, and not spent on other purposes. However, witnesses Ji Yunqing, and the Zou Chengtai factory owners, Zou Jikang, Fu Weisong, and Fan et al., all unanimously stated that Zhu Xiongwu was indeed present when the settlement was reached, reviewing all the documents for Jiang Hongbin. The Zou brothers stated that they did not initially know who Zhu was, but only knew that he had been invited by Jiang, and later learned that he was Secretary Zhu from the Jiangsu High Court. Zhu, however, claimed that the clothing described by Zou and Ji as what he was wearing on that day differed slightly, and therefore claimed that the witnesses' testimony was inconsistent, proving that he was not actually in Wuxi that day. The court, noting that Ji and Zou had no animosity towards Zhu, and were now all saying that Zhu was present at the reconciliation, repeatedly questioned Zhu. Zhu vehemently denied participating in the mediation. Ji Yunqing also stated that he had not received any monetary reward. Next, Zhu Xinfu's letter instructing Lu Wenguang to contact the parties involved was examined. The letter was found during a search of Lu's home, and the envelope was from the Jiangsu High Court. Lu previously stated that the letter was written as a joke by his nephew. Today, the seventeen-year-old child, Ru Yide, appeared in court and testified that he was studying in Suzhou and living at Lu's home. This letter was written when he was fifteen years old. The contents were merely a transcription of casual conversations he overheard at Lu's house from litigants, written as an exercise to practice letter writing. Furthermore, there was no such person as Zhu Xinfu. However, the words "awaiting reply" and the signature on the envelope were not written by me. Next, Miao Wenye and Cheng Jiu were examined regarding the public prosecution by the prosecutor in the Jiangsu High Court for offenses against national currency. Witnesses Miao and Ye both firmly stated that they did not know Zhu, and that there was no request for assistance or anything of the sort. Judge Huang then granted Chen Chaozuan bail of 500 yuan, remanded Zhu and Lu in custody, and rescheduled the hearing for next Monday afternoon.

Accusation of Liu Huizhi for Embezzlement of Bank Funds and Infringement of Shareholder Rights: Claiming 4 to 5 Million Yuan

Zhang Chongfu filed a confirmation lawsuit in the Civil Court.

He Jiechun and others submitted seven pieces of evidence of embezzlement.

—The Defendant was absent due to suffering from neurasthenia—

Liu Huizhi, the former chairman and manager of the China Industrial Bank and a native of Anhui, has been accused by shareholder Zhang Chongfu of embezzling public funds during his tenure, thereby infringing upon the rights of shareholders. Zhang filed a criminal complaint with the First Special Court. After deliberation, the court determined that Zhang's right to sue needed to be confirmed first in the Civil Court, and suspended the criminal trial. Zhang followed the instructions and filed a confirmation lawsuit in the Civil Court, which has now ruled in favor of confirming Zhang's right to sue.

Liu appealed this verdict to the Second Branch of the High Court, where the proceedings are ongoing. Now, another wave arises. Five more shareholders of the China Industrial Bank, He Jiechun, Weng Pengnian, Zhu Ruping, Yan Shu, and Yan Xiaoquan (holding a total of 640 shares worth 64,000 yuan), have discovered

evidence of Liu's embezzlement

in as many as seven instances, damaging bank funds by approximately 4 to 5 million yuan. The bank originally held shares in the Beiping Waterworks Company, with a face value of 200,500 yuan. These shares were purchased at a price of 165 yuan per thousand, for a total value of 33,825 yuan in national currency. On June 3, 1932, Liu unilaterally increased the purchase price of these shares by 245 yuan per thousand, increasing the cost by 50,225 yuan. On the same day, the increased amount was paid out of the bank under the guise of legitimate expenses, and simultaneously deposited into a "Gong Shun Ji" account opened by Liu under an assumed name. In one fell swoop, he

embezzled bank funds

of 50,225 yuan. On August 5, 1929, Liu falsely created a "Heng Ji" account in the savings department of the China Industrial Bank and deposited 30,000 yuan. On the same day, 29,500 yuan was withdrawn. Although there were subsequent deposits, the withdrawals always matched. Therefore, at the end of 1929, the account showed a balance of 500 yuan with an interest rate of six percent. By January 3, 1930, the account suddenly ballooned to a massive 360,013.80 yuan by January 18th. An investigation revealed that this money did not belong to Heng Ji at all. It was Liu who falsely created the Heng Ji account,

claiming to represent

the bank. The bank issued banknotes of 40,000 yuan per day, for a period of ten days. Liu deposited the banknote funds into the bank, achieving his purpose of private gain and embezzlement of profits. In total, he embezzled 23,666.14 yuan in interest. Liu purchased 1.569 mu of land on Avenue Edouard VII, intending to build a residence. Then, on May 25, 1931, Liu raised the price of the land to 112,000 taels and sold it to Heng Shun Company (which he had established). Heng Shun then transferred it to Daheng Company at the original price. Daheng then used this land, along with four other title deeds, to mortgage 224,140.23 taels to Heng Shun. Daheng then redeemed the land on Avenue Edouard VII with 70,000 taels. Ultimately, by using Heng Shun, he sold the land to the bank for 120,000 taels, offsetting the debt. His actions were nothing more than

creating a smokescreen

to achieve his purpose of damaging bank funds, causing the bank to lose 98,550 taels. Liu caused the bank to lose more than 42,000 taels with 2.188 mu of land on North Henan Road. He also caused the bank to lose 19,754.10 taels with 2.554 mu of land on Xin Zha Road. On January 7, 1932, due to the bank issuing too many banknotes, Liu feared inspection by the Ministry of Finance. He deposited 500,000 yuan of the bank's banknotes into a special deposit account under the name of Fa Ji, in order to reduce the amount of banknotes issued. Liu then took the opportunity to convert the deposit into a loan item on behalf of the Zhong Ji account,

collecting interest

at a monthly rate of seven percent, resulting in an annual interest payment of 42,000 yuan. The office in the French Concession had a "Zu Ji" account, used to store rent collected by Sun Yangnong on behalf of the bank for purchased properties. As of the end of June 1932, a total of 11,619.07 taels in rent had been received. After paying attorney Lu 50 taels, the whereabouts of the remaining 7,517 taels belonging to the head office are unknown. As manager, Liu cannot shirk his responsibility. After investigating these seven items, He et al. hired attorneys Chen Ying and Tang Yan to file a criminal complaint of embezzlement against Liu. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Tan of the First Special Court opened the first criminal court for the hearing. Liu Huizhi was absent. His attorney appeared in court and stated that Liu was suffering from

neurasthenia

and was being treated at a sanatorium in Shanghai, and therefore could not attend the hearing. He requested that the hearing be postponed and asked for the case file of Zhang Chongfu to be retrieved. The plaintiff's attorneys, however, stated that they were now

adding Li Jizhi, the managing director of the China Industrial Bank, as a defendant. After Judge Tan reviewed the report, he ordered that the hearing be rescheduled because the case file still needed to be retrieved.

City Residents Should Be Careful About Their Diet: Gastroenteritis Cases Have Been Discovered

Spring infectious diseases have disappeared. Era Hospitals are busily preparing.

The weather in this city suddenly turned hot and humid on the 13th, and the heat remains high today, fully expressing the summer climate. The situation is recorded below:

Cases of Gastroenteritis Discovered

Since the start of summer in this port city, the weather has been cool, resulting in the continued presence of spring infectious diseases on the market. Since the sudden shift to hot weather beginning on the 13th, infectious diseases have begun to disappear over the past three days and have not been heard of. However, the number of people sleeping on the streets and those who greedily consume cold food has gradually increased, leading to the occurrence of summer epidemics such as gastroenteritis, especially among coolies. Therefore, people should be very careful about their diet to avoid suffering from illness.

Era Hospital Opens

This year is one of the most likely years for the outbreak of epidemics. Therefore, the establishment of epidemic hospitals is extremely important. Currently, in addition to the Shanghai Era Hospital on Xizang Road, which operates year-round, the Emergency Epidemic Hospital on North Xizang Road is also actively preparing to open as usual. The Chinese Epidemic Hospital on Huade Road in Hongkou opened yesterday at 2:00 PM, providing day and night consultation and accommodation, with 120 beds available.

Yu Yuexiu Temporarily Returned to Biological Mother for Adoption

Yu Minquan (38 years old, from Ningbo, currently doing business outside), and his wife Yu Zheng, residing in Xiaomuzhiqiao, Xietu Road, in the Chinese Concession, have a daughter named Xiuyue, who is fourteen years old this year. On June 11th of last year, through relatives Zheng Ahong and Wang Zhoushi as matchmakers, she was betrothed to Zheng Chunli (24 years old this year, continuing his father's singing business, previously performing at the Xinguang Grand Theater, now taking gigs at home), the son of Zheng Yuekui (58 years old, engaged in opera singing), and Zheng Qiu (53 years old, usually a vegetarian who chants Buddhist scriptures), residing at No. 13 Qiaoan Lane, Avenue d'Aligre, in the French Concession. At that time, they received a bride price of 80 yuan. Xiuyue then entered the family as a child bride. Unexpectedly, her aunt Zheng Qiu, although usually a vegetarian who chants Buddhist scriptures, was of violent nature. Seeing that her adopted daughter-in-law was young and unable to handle adult work, she often abused her. When the victim Yu Xiuyue testified about the abuse she had suffered, she cried incessantly. Judge Li reviewed the testimony and ordered that the hearing be rescheduled for the morning of the 18th. The victim was ordered to go to the forensic doctor for examination and was temporarily returned to her biological mother, Yu Zheng, for adoption.

Dinh Vệ Hưng Sentenced to Six Months in Prison for Seducing a Young Woman

Dinh Vệ Hưng (24 years old, from Wuxi) opened a Wufeng vermicelli shop in the Wang Zhu establishment. On the evening of December 3rd of the previous year, at 11 p.m., he seduced Ji Fen, the 18-year-old daughter, and took her to a Suzhou hotel, where he locked her in a room and had sexual intercourse with her. After staying for a week, they went to Jiaxing, rented a house, and lived together like husband and wife for five months. She became pregnant. Last April, he sent the girl home and told her to reveal the situation to her mother. Wang Zhu was furious, saw her daughter's abdomen protruding, scolded her and drove her out. The girl regretted her actions and sought out Dinh again, and they temporarily rented a small house in the south city. In September, she gave birth to a child. Recently, they returned to his home in Wuxi, where she learned that her master had a wife. Unwilling to be a concubine, they disagreed and resented each other. Feeling resentful, she and Dinh came to Shanghai the day before and went to her house to beg her mother. Wang Zhu felt that Dinh should not have harmed her daughter to such an extent, ruining her lifelong happiness. She secretly reported to the Yangshupu Police Station, which dispatched Chinese detective Wang Renzhong to rush to arrest Dinh and bring him to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the third criminal court of the First Special Court, where Labor Bureau attorney Zhang Shuaizhu filed a public prosecution for the crime of disrupting marriage and requested investigation. Wang Zhu proved the defendant's seduction process. The judge asked the young woman Ji Fen to state that she was weak-minded and deceived at the time, and that she did not want to follow him, etc. Dinh pleaded guilty, stating that the child was currently being raised at his home in Wuxi. Xiao Xiefen ruled to sentence Dinh to six months imprisonment as a warning.

There were a total of eight victims. He also confessed that his accomplices, Wang Liansheng (28 years old, from Suzhou), were hiding in a den on No. 147 Luxiang Road. According to Wang Liansheng, the stolen goods were sold by Dong Dalu (43 years old, from Haimen). He was hiding at No. 180 Luxiang Road in the city. They arrested Huang and took him to the team. On the way, they passed the used goods beach on Guanyinge Street, Xinkai River, and arrested the receiver Zhu Wang, and brought them to the team for interrogation. They sent personnel to various places to retrieve the original victims. The seven thieves, along with the stolen goods, were transferred to the Sixteen Shop Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Revenge Untaken, Calamity Strikes Again

Jin Xingsheng and Others Detained and Brought to Court, Further Investigation Scheduled for This Friday

Jin Xingsheng from Shanghai and his party, who ran a laundry business, went to the Tianyun Lou amusement park at the Wing On Company on the 16th of last month. At the civilized play theater, a dispute arose with a tea server named A'gang over tea. Jin was immediately beaten severely by A'gang and others. Subsequently, A'gang's father and a female tea server from the Shaoxing opera theater at the amusement park, nicknamed Da A, intervened to mediate and offered Jin face. After the show, Da A accompanied Jin to Changsha Road, but unexpectedly, Da A gathered more people and severely beat Jin again. Feeling deeply resentful after these two beatings, Jin constantly sought revenge. Yesterday, he gathered Ma Jinhai from Tongzhou, Zhu Quanyuan from Haimen, Zhang Zhirong from Shaoxing, and Xu Zigao from Tongzhou, a total of four people, and went to Room 13 of the Hongxiang Inn, No. 20 Aivenyi Road, to discuss methods of revenge. They also brought three axes. However, the plan was discovered by Chinese detectives Wang Jiaju and Chen Shanji from the Old Zha gate Police Station, who, along with Western Detective Smith, arrested them at 9:55 PM the previous evening. Ma Jinhai was arrested inside the room, and the three axes were confiscated and taken back to the police station. Detectives remained on guard in the room. At 10:10 PM, Jin, Zhu, Zhang, and Xu arrived and were arrested together. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Special District Court, Criminal Division 1. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the situation, stating that the case required further investigation and requesting detention. Detective Wang then submitted a report on the arrest. Judge Qian Hongye reviewed the report and questioned the five suspects briefly, ordering their detention until this Friday for further interrogation.

Seduction and Abandonment

Vice President of Zhongnan Bank, Yang Zhongfen, Accused

Demanding 20,000 Yuan for Living and Educational Expenses, Defendant Absent, Hearing Rescheduled for Wednesday

Liu Huizhen, a 22-year-old woman from Suzhou residing at No. 58, Xin Xiude Lane, Baike Road, recently retained a lawyer to file a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the First Special Court, accusing Yang Zhongfen, Vice President of Zhongnan Bank, of seduction and abandonment. The lawsuit included a civil claim, requesting the court to order the defendant to pay 10,000 yuan for living expenses and 10,000 yuan for the upbringing and education of their biological son, A'li. The court had already heard the case several times but had to reschedule each time due to the defendant's absence. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang held another session in the criminal court. The defendant still failed to appear. His defense lawyer stated that the defendant was scheduled to return to Shanghai from another port by ship today to surrender to the court and respond to the charges, but he had not yet arrived. It was presumed that the ship was delayed due to fog, so he requested another postponement. He presented an airmail letter written by the defendant as evidence. The plaintiff, Liu Huizhen, holding her son A'li, testified that she was sold by her mother to a brothel run by a foster mother named Chen A'liu (located at Xiaohuayuan, Sanma Road) at the age of seventeen and worked as a prostitute. The defendant, Yang Zhongfen, was a customer. After their relationship began, he claimed that his wife had passed away and expressed his desire to marry her. On December 10th of the 22nd year of the Republic, he forbade her from continuing to work as a prostitute and arranged a private elopement. They first resided at the Hongkou Grand Hotel. At that time, the defendant instructed her to hire lawyer Li Mingsen to send a letter to Chen A'liu to negotiate, but she did not file a lawsuit due to her conscience. Subsequently, they rented a place at Yongfeng Lane on North Sichuan Road, and later moved to No. 39, Sheng Dali, Shengmuyuan Road in the French Concession. For several years, all expenses were covered by the defendant. When she became pregnant two years ago, the defendant arranged for her to give birth at the Ke Mei Obstetrics Hospital. However, at the end of last year, she learned that the defendant already had a wife. After expressing some criticism, the defendant changed his attitude, cut off financial support, and stopped visiting. Therefore, she filed the lawsuit, requesting the court to order him to pay 20,000 yuan. Judge Jiang reviewed the testimony and ordered the case to be rescheduled for next Wednesday afternoon.

Bathhouse Owner and Lawyer Accused of Joint Fraud

Zhang Yubao, former owner of the Furun Chi bathhouse at the intersection of Ximen, Zhonghua Road, and Penglai Road, found it difficult to maintain operations due to poor business in April of this year. He entrusted lawyer Zhang Binqiu, residing at No. 21, Lafayette Road, French Concession, to act as his agent with full authority to clear accounts and solicit the transfer of the bathhouse. Subsequently, Wu Shicui, a local resident of Dongxinqiao Street, French Concession, contacted lawyer Zhang to negotiate the transfer, with a price of 1,450 yuan, of which 900 yuan was for off-the-books costs and 590 yuan was for remuneration. Lawyer Zhang guaranteed that there would be no unexpected disputes. Both parties signed a contract and paid the transfer price. Suddenly, the landlord, Wang Caibao, opposed the transfer due to Furun Chi's unpaid rent. He appointed lawyer Wang Kanghou and filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai District Court, which issued a preliminary injunction in May, sealing the Furun Chi bathhouse. Wu Shicui, having taken over the bathhouse, was unable to operate and lost the transfer price. He contacted lawyer Zhang and the former owner, Zhang Yubao, to negotiate, but to no avail. Wu then filed a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court, accusing Zhang Yubao and lawyer Zhang Binqiu of fraud, requesting that they be investigated and prosecuted according to the law, and seeking the return of the paid transfer price. The court, based on the lawsuit, held a hearing and ordered a postponement. Yesterday morning, another hearing was held. The defendant, Zhang Binqiu, filed a countersuit accusing Wu of defamation and obstruction of reputation. The plaintiff, Wu, presented the case as described above. After questioning the two defendants, the court, believing the facts were clear, ordered closing arguments and announced that the verdict would be delivered at noon on the 22nd.

District Court Burns Large Quantity of Opium Yesterday

The Shanghai District Court, from July of the 24th year of the Republic to April of this year, confiscated 94 packages of opium of various sizes, weighing 354 catties gross, as well as 8 packages of opium, weighing 706 taels, 6 boxes of red pills, 1 package of morphine, a small amount of opium paste in 11 small boxes plus one piece, a small package of opium, 109 opium bubbles, one small package and one half-small box of opium ash in two small packages, and one box weighing one tael including the box, 289 pieces of opium paraphernalia and opium bubbles and ash, and one set of opium paraphernalia. All items were sealed and the quantities specified were counted by item. The case was presented to the Jiangsu High Court Procuratorate, which designated 2:00 PM yesterday as the time to burn the items in the courtyard of the court. Representatives from various agencies who attended to supervise included Zhan Yufen from the High Court Procuratorate, Tang Peiyou and Ju Zhijing from the First Special Court, Qiao Wanxuan and Zheng Ziying from the Second Special Court, Guo Lanxin from the Headquarters, Ren Bin from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Lu Youchang from the Jianghai Customs, Ma Mingzu from the Municipal Government, and Wu Hefang from the Municipal Police Bureau. They were welcomed by Court President Luo and Chief Justice Zhong, who ordered police chiefs Zhang Shuping and Chen Xihui to supervise the destruction of the narcotics in public. The ashes were dumped into the Huangpu River to eliminate the toxic atmosphere.

He Shengrong Arrested for Peddling Fake Seasoning Powder

He Shengrong, 37, from Changshu, had no steady job. Recently, he had a fanciful idea: he went to various used bottle shops to buy large quantities of used empty bottles of Weizong and Ajinomoto, filled them with starch powder, and covered the top with a little Ajinomoto and various other seasoning powders. He peddled them in various vegetable markets, asking one dime per bottle, but also accepting eleven copper coins. Many of the buyers in the vegetable markets were ignorant maids, and they were greedy for the cheap price and because the powder at the bottle opening tasted delicious, so countless people were deceived. Yesterday, the scam was discovered in Wujiaochang, Caojiadu, and the local police arrested him, seizing the starch and 29 bottles of fake seasoning powder, and took him to the station for interrogation.

Shanghai Experienced a Downpour Yesterday, Humidity Eased After the Rain

Since the 13th, the weather in Shanghai had suddenly turned hot and muggy, and the climate yesterday and the day before remained hot and stifling. Around noon yesterday, a sudden downpour occurred, lasting for thirty minutes. After 2:00 PM, the sunlight shone through, the sky cleared, and the easterly wind blew, easing the humidity somewhat.

Merchants and Residents of Xujiahui Request Filling in the Li Zongjing River Channel

The Li Zongjing River channel behind Xujiahui, west of Shanghai, connects to the Pu Zhao River in the south and reaches Fahua Town in the north. It has not been dredged since it was dredged in the 7th year of the Republic, and silt has accumulated. In recent years, residents along the river have dumped garbage into it daily, causing the current to stop flowing, the water to turn black as ink, and a foul odor to spread, making people nauseous. Now that summer has arrived, mosquitoes swarm, which is a significant health hazard. Various groups in Fahua Township have repeatedly petitioned the authorities to fill in the channel, but no action has been taken. Now, over two hundred merchants and residents of the Gelu area of Xujiahui have jointly petitioned the Municipal Government, requesting that the Public Works Bureau quickly fill in the river once and for all, both to revitalize the market and to sell the land for public benefit.

The petition has been noted, and the Shanghai Municipal Government has been consulted to investigate and handle the matter." This notice was issued.

China Merchants Inland River Steamship Bureau: Shareholder Registration Deadline

The Donghui Meeting Scheduled for the 25th

The Bureau Has a Total of Nineteen Small Steamships

The China Merchants Inland River Steamship Bureau has suffered significant losses and heavy debts over the years. At the same time, due to the development of inland highways, passenger and cargo transportation has mostly shifted from water to land, making operations very difficult. The bureau has decided to convene a shareholders' meeting on the 25th of this month to discuss ways to improve the situation. The details have been reported in the newspapers. Here are the follow-up details:

Registration Deadline

Since the bureau published a notice to all shareholders holding shares to bring their shares to the China Merchants Bureau to register and receive admission tickets for the meeting, it is said that not many shareholders went to the bureau to register. The reason is probably that the Inland River Bureau was established a long time ago, and shareholders have transferred shares many times, and many have been lost. The shareholder registration period was scheduled to end at 5:00 PM yesterday and will not be extended. The shareholders' meeting will be held as scheduled on the 25th. According to sources, there is no hope for a turnaround in inland river operations, so the China Merchants authorities have decided to close it down. Most of the small inland river ships will be auctioned off to pay off debts.

Small Ship Names

It is known that the China Merchants Inland River Steamship Bureau used to have a total of twenty-one small ships on each line. Except for the Gonglong, which sank in the early years, and the Hengfeng, which was also dismantled due to its old hull, there are now only nineteen ships. Their names are as follows: Xiangfu, Lichuan, He'an, Jianyuan, Hekuan, Hengtong, Junfa, Liheng, Liyuan, Hengsheng, Hengji, Hengren, Feilong, Hejun, Taichang, Xinan, Ruishun, Lihang, Feiniao. In addition, there are sixteen tugboats and four cargo ships, totaling thirty-nine ships.

Evaluation of the Achievements of the Vehicle Committee Two Years After its Establishment

Improved Rickshaw Pullers' Lives and More Pleasant-Looking Vehicles

Lowered Vehicle Rental Fees Benefit Rickshaw Pullers and Do Not Harm Vehicle Owners

The Public Concession authorities, due to the need to improve the rickshaw situation in the city, organized a Special Rickshaw Committee in September 1933 to investigate and study various aspects of the rickshaw problem and propose improvement measures. By February of the following year, the committee had completed its investigation, prepared a report, and submitted it to the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department, along with sixteen recommendations. Subsequently, the Public Works Department convened a joint meeting of the Security and Transportation Committee to discuss the report and its various recommendations for improvement. As a result, the joint meeting advocated the establishment of a Rickshaw Affairs Committee and adopted thirteen of the improvement measures proposed by the Special Committee. The Public Works Department's Rickshaw Affairs Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Vehicle Committee) was established on May 23, 1934, and appointed Westerner Mr. Massey (former director of the Public Works Department) and Chinese Zhu Maocheng, Wang Zhiren, and Mr. Jun as members. It began operations immediately, implementing the improvement matters recommended by the Special Committee. Now, the Vehicle Committee has been established for two years, and all facilities have been announced and reported in Chinese and foreign newspapers. Recently, the Vehicle Committee prepared a report on the achievements of its work over the past two years and submitted it to the Board of Directors, comparing the improvement items originally approved by the Board of Directors with the extent to which the committee has achieved them. We have learned the content and selectively disclose it, which should be welcomed by those who are concerned about social issues.

The original recommendation No. 4, "The existing 10,000 public rickshaw licenses will not be reduced for the time being. However, the Rickshaw Affairs Committee may at any time present articles to the Board of Directors to gradually reduce the number of rickshaw licenses," has been contributed by the Vehicle Committee to the Special Rickshaw Committee and is still under consideration by the Special Committee.

The original recommendation No. 5, "The vehicle owner registration book, as recently compiled, should be put into effect as soon as possible," has now been satisfactorily completed.

The original recommendation No. 6, "Implement regulations on vehicle rental fees, register rickshaw pullers, and improve vehicles so that rickshaw pullers can increase their income and improve their living conditions," now the vehicle rental fee has been set and magnetic plates have been nailed next to the vehicles, specifying the amount of the fare. However, when rickshaw pullers and passengers negotiate their own prices, it is difficult to make both parties abide by the official fare. Furthermore, rickshaw pullers are now generally registered and vehicles are gradually being improved, and the establishment of rickshaw puller mutual aid societies can be said to have achieved considerable results in the eyes of the Vehicle Committee. The benefits that mutual aid societies can now offer to rickshaw pullers include: children's schools, outdoor and indoor clinics, injury and sickness relief, insurance, funeral expenses, public cemeteries, bathing facilities, dormitories, canteens, and tea rooms. Roughly calculated, if a rickshaw puller's physical strength has not declined, then what he earns now is one dollar and seventy cents to two dollars and forty cents more per month than two years ago, and the various benefits provided by the mutual aid society are not included.

The original recommendation No. 7, "Public and private rickshaw pullers should be registered and licensed immediately," the registration and licensing of public and private rickshaw pullers has now been satisfactorily completed, and rickshaw pullers have recently been re-registered to meet the needs of the rickshaw industry.

The original recommendation No. 8, "The public rickshaw rental fee should be calculated at eight dimes for a full 24 hours, or pro-rated based on the length of time. The Board of Directors of the Public Works Department may modify these rental fees at any time." The vehicle rental fee has now been reduced to seven dimes and seven cents per day (including seven cents for mutual aid society fees). This rent reduction benefits rickshaw pullers and does not increase the suffering of vehicle owners.

The original recommendation No. 9, "Specify vehicle rental fees based on the distance of the road and the length of time, and list them in a conspicuous place on the vehicle," has now been achieved. This price list is calculated in dimes, but the Vehicle Committee is not currently advocating changing the new table.

The original recommendation No. 10, "Public rickshaw vehicles should be improved immediately," now there are a total of 1,765 new-style vehicles on the market. According to the Vehicle Committee, these new-style vehicles are far superior to the old-style vehicles in terms of comfort and weather protection. According to a survey from the rickshaw pullers' side, the new-style vehicles are stable and convenient to drive.

The original recommendation No. 11, "Vehicle inspections should be stricter than before," much has already been done, and there is still much to be done. This depends on the efforts of the staff.

The original recommendation No. 13, "Establish rickshaw stations in convenient locations everywhere," there are now 91 rickshaw parking places within the Public Concession, most of which have been established in the last two years.

The original recommendation No. 14, "The rickshaw registration method should be improved," has now been achieved. It is now planned to formulate a method that allows the Public Works Department to revoke the licenses of rickshaw pullers who do not perform their duties on time, so as to avoid unqualified individuals.

The original recommendation No. 15, "Continue to crack down on 'wild' chartered vehicles," this is being actively cracked down on.

"Q&A on Postal Knowledge" is Selling Well

The "China Post" by Zhang Zhiren, a renowned authority on postal studies, has been popular since the publication of the upper and middle volumes (Commercial Press University Series). Now, in response to the request of general readers, he has specially compiled the book "Q&A on Postal Knowledge," which has been in its third edition since its release in May of this year. If not for the low price (fifty-five cents), rich content (two hundred pages), and the author's high reputation, how could this be achieved? In Shanghai, the book is sold by the China Book Company, Kaiming Bookstore, Life Bookstore, Shanghai Magazine Company, China Book Company, and other bookstores. In other cities, it is sold by Commercial Press in various places. This book is not only a shortcut to understanding the content of China's postal service, but also an essential reading for postal examinations.

City News

Publication of the National Air Defense Illustrated Guide: Yang Peiwen of the New Era Publishing House, aware of the increasingly urgent situation in the Far East, collected knowledge about air defense from various countries to reduce the suffering of compatriots during wartime, such as the performance and identification methods of various aircraft, the characteristics of various aircraft actions, the identification methods of aircraft from various countries, the performance and avoidance methods of killing bombs, destruction bombs, incendiary bombs, and gas bombs, the construction methods of various anti-virus equipment, simple basements, and detailed architectural plans for precision basements, air raid warnings and actions after hearing the warning, the implementation plan for light control, air defense buildings, and various air defense weapons, etc. A total of 94 items are listed, and each item is drawn with vivid pictures, and supplemented with simple texts for detailed explanation, so even those who have a little knowledge of characters can understand it at a glance. The entire book has a total of 102 pages, 10 inches long and 7 inches wide, and the opposite side is a five-color printed air force night battle map, which is exciting. Now, the museum is charging only 20 cents of national currency per copy to recover the cost, with no intention of making a profit, for the purpose of popularizing among the people. The general wholesale office and mail order address is No. 1 Jiuxingfang, Zhangjia Street, Sanpailou, Shanghai, and it is soliciting the establishment of distribution offices in various provinces, cities, and prosperous cities. Those who are interested in undertaking this business are welcome to contact us by mail.

Publication of the 4th Issue of Military Intelligence Pictorial: The "World Military Intelligence Pictorial" published by the World Military Intelligence Agency at No. 2, Lane 514, Ladou Road, this city, has been beautifully printed and has excellent content since the first issue was reprinted in photo-offset version. Subscribers from all walks of life are very enthusiastic. In addition to community groups, schools, and individuals, there are also subscriptions in the military, including the army, navy, and air force, all over 19 provinces and cities. After the third issue was reprinted, the fourth issue has now been published, and the content is even more exciting. The main items are "Today's World," "The Confrontation Between Japan and the Soviet Union and the Sacrifices in the Crossfire," "The International Situation After Germany Abrogated the Treaty," "The Cause and Effect of the German Army Re-entering the Rhineland," "The French Maginot Line and Eastern Border Defense," "World Military Intelligence Current Affairs Atlas," all of which are accompanied by detailed explanations and detailed maps. Other topics such as "National Defense Science" are important treatises for the revival of the nation, "Future Air Battles" introduces the secret light of death and various air combat weapons, "Air Combat Strategy and Tactics," and "American Air Flagship" reveal the air force strength of various countries. In addition, there is also "Wartime Raw Material Problems," explaining the necessity of preparing for a rainy day. The military intelligence novel about the future Japanese-American war, "Undeclared War," is even more rich in materials related to our country's national destiny. Although the retail price is 30 cents per copy, and the annual price is 3 yuan and 60 cents in national currency, one page is worth the cost of the entire book. All military personnel and people should prepare for reference.

Publication of the Innovation Issue of Women's Monthly: The Women's Monthly, edited by the Shanghai Women's Education Center on Hualong Road, is a publication that explores women's issues. It is reported that the fifth issue of the second volume was published yesterday. In addition to the original text in each column, a serial picture column has been added, with popular text and profound discussions. It is an indispensable reading material for women. The price is 10 cents per copy, and it is sold in major magazine companies and newsstands.

Our Country's World Games Football Team European Travel Notes Written and Sent by Li Huitang

On May 26th, after our narrow victory over the Malang players, because the weather was cool and the scenery was pleasant, "Autumn enters the heat at twelve o'clock", which is most suitable for recuperation, we decided to stay for two days. Our team's decision to go on a long expedition and fight hard for days, now let's do a general review of the injured. Huang Jiliang, Li Guowei, and Chen Zhenhe injured their ankles, Huang Meiyu and Zheng Jiliang injured their knees, the reporter injured his shoulder, and there were many minor injuries. Fortunately, in this area with water and soil not suitable for everyone, no one has contracted a disease, which can be regarded as the blessing of Heaven. On the 28th, we returned to Surabaya by special car. There was nothing to say overnight. On the 29th at noon, we took the train to Yishi Long. When we arrived at the station, all the houses were lit up. The whole team moved into the China Hotel. On the 30th, early in the morning, Huitang and Director Rong went to the airport to meet Manager Huang Jiajun, because he had to stay in Surabaya to settle accounts, so he took a plane early this morning. At 10 o'clock, we were jointly welcomed by the local Kuomintang branch, the General Chamber of Commerce, and various overseas Chinese organizations, who presented flags and gave instructions, just like the earnest expectations of overseas Chinese in other cities. Finally, the reporter and Dr. Rong gave speeches one after another. The tea party was photographed, and then the meeting was dismissed. At 5 o'clock in the afternoon, we competed with the Long Selection Team. The opponent's strength was weak and could not withstand a single blow. As a result, our team was able to do whatever it wanted and wantonly destroy them with a score of 9-0, making the opponent unable to fight back. The fans were happy to go home. Our team used a new formation to respond in this battle as follows: three to zero in the first half, and nine to zero in the end. The goalscorers were Jingxiang 3, Jinshun and Jiangbai 2 each, and Beihua and Guicheng 1 each. The acting captain, Bao Jiaping, felt plain and not nervous. The football level of Longchuan is the weakest among the major ports in Java. Its basic selection team also sent teachers to Surabaya to participate in the All-Java Football Port Championship. Those who faced us today were even worse. However, in the first 25 minutes of the first half, they were able to resist tenaciously. Their spirit of hard work is admirable. The lineup of our team changed greatly on this day, because most of the central defenders were injured. Wenli and Xianyuan were originally central defenders, and today they were used to fill the vacancy. They were also familiar with the job and performed well. However, the opponent's strength was too weak and it was difficult to make a true test. Our countermeasures on the stage were improper, and we failed to attack repeatedly. It was not until 25 minutes later that we opened the record. In the second half, the opposing team was too tired and their exhausted expressions were fully revealed, and it became our team's world. The fish and meat on the chopping board were slaughtered at will. The game ended with a score of 9-0. If the breakthrough in the first half had not been too late, I am afraid that the number of losses on the other side would have been more than this. The mayor presented the trophy and dispersed after three cheers.

Zhejiang Province Determines the Date of the High School Entrance Examination to be Held on July 12 in Separate Districts

The 24th Academic Year Second High School Graduation Examination Committee of the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education held its first meeting at the Department of Education yesterday (13th) at 10:00 a.m. More than 10 people including Xu Xudong and Jin Jianqing attended. Graduates will register from June 29 to June 30, the entrance examination will be held on July 12, and the papers will be graded from July 3 to 18. The high school scores will be calculated by July 17 and the junior high school scores will be calculated by July 20. Guangdong Education Department Implements Subsidy Measures for Free Education

(Guangzhou Correspondence) The Guangdong Education Department has been promoting free education in recent years, and progress has been rapid. There are two sources of funding: one is to request subsidies from the provincial and central treasuries, and the other is to stipulate that counties and cities raise their own funds locally. For those who apply for subsidies to establish schools, the salaries of vocational teachers are fully allocated by the central government or the province. Counties and cities are only responsible for planning establishment fees and office expenses. Those who establish schools through their own fundraising are responsible for the salaries of vocational teachers, establishment fees, and office expenses. The Education Department now considers that the previous subsidy method was of a promotional nature, while the principle of promoting free education is to encourage counties and cities to organize it themselves, establish more primary schools, and broaden enrollment. Therefore, starting from the 25th year of the Republic (1936), new subsidy methods will be promulgated, and the original Provisional Measures for Implementing Free Education will be specially revised. The main points are as follows:

Subsidized primary schools before the 24th year of the Republic (1935) will continue to be handled as before. Starting from the 25th year of the Republic (1936), subsidies will be provided based on the economic situation of each county and city, classified into different grades. 1. First-class counties: Nanhai, Panyu, Dongguan, Shunde, Zhongshan, Xinhui, Chao'an, Chaoyang, Jieyang, Gaoyao, Taishan, Qujiang, Qiongshan, Maoming, Yangjiang, Qingyuan, Huiyang, Hepu, and other counties, as well as Shantou City, will receive an annual subsidy of 25% of the total cost of newly established county and municipal short-term primary schools. Counties and cities will raise 75% themselves. 2. Second-class counties: Meixian, Kaiping, Wenchang, Xingning, Chenghai, Haikang, Luoding, Xinyi, Lufeng, Haifeng, Yingde, Lianjiang, Boluo, Guangning, Raoping, Heyuan, Yangchun, Huaxian, Zengcheng, Puning, Nanxiong, Dianbai, Wuhua, Yunfu, Sanshui, Qinxian, Fangcheng, Lingshan, and other counties, as well as Meilu City, will receive an annual subsidy of 50% of the total cost of newly established county and municipal short-term primary schools. Counties and cities will raise 50% themselves. 3. Third-class counties: Heshan, Pu, Enping, Conghua, Lechang, Lianxian, Jiaoling, Sihui, Xinxing, Ding'an, Chengmai, Suixi, Huilai, Danxian, Deqing, Longchuan, Yunan, Zijin, Yaxian, Wanning, Huaxian, Shixing, Lingao, Pingyuan, Wuchuan, Longmen, Changming, Renhua, Fengshun, Heping, Bao'an, Wengyuan, Lianping, Fogang, Xinfeng, Xuwen, Lingshui, Fengchuan, Lianshan, Yangshan, and other counties will receive an annual subsidy of 75% of the total cost of newly established county short-term primary schools. Counties will raise 25% themselves. 4. Special third-class counties: Qiongdong, Chixi, Gan'en, Changjiang, Lehui, Kaijian, Ruyuan, Nan'ao　counties will receive an annual subsidy of 90% of the total cost of newly established short-term primary schools. Counties will raise 10% themselves. The subsidy funds for Baoting, Ledong, Baisha, and three other counties, as well as the Nanshan Administration and the Yunyao Bureau, will be handled separately. After the 25th year of the Republic (1936), the county governments may, based on the local economic situation, request the Education Department to approve changes to the distribution of subsidies for newly established short-term primary schools in each county and city. The teachers and staff of the primary schools shall also be selected and appointed by the county and city governments themselves, but they must submit their resumes to the Education Department for approval.

Shenmei Girls' Middle and Primary School in this city has hired Fan Mingyao as principal after reorganizing its internal structure. The school site was insufficient, so it moved to a new school building in a Western-style house at the intersection of North Henan Road and Avenue Edward VII the other day. The school's 10th anniversary celebration will be held on the 21st of this month, and a summer school has begun enrollment, with free tuition for all grades in junior high and primary school.

Children's Education and the National Salvation Movement (2)

A Speech by Municipal Education Director Pan Gongzhan on the Central Radio Station

If we can truly follow this educational purpose and achieve the goal of "enriching people's lives, supporting social survival, developing national livelihoods, and continuing people's lives," so that the nation can truly be independent, civil rights can truly be universal, and people's livelihoods can truly be developed, then education will have done its utmost in saving the nation. Originally, the Premier said, "The Three Principles of the People are the doctrine of national salvation." A doctrine can only be based on one. Since we are now using the sole Three Principles of the People to save the nation, build the nation, and govern the nation, education cannot jump outside the scope of the nation and, of course, can only be based on this sole Three Principles of the People and cannot be compatible with other doctrines. It can be seen that the education of the Three Principles of the People is indeed national salvation education and the only national salvation education. Why do we need to come up with new tricks?

Furthermore, in terms of the goals of primary school education, the overall goal of our Chinese primary school education is: "Primary schools should, based on the Three Principles of the People, and in accordance with the educational purpose and implementation policies of the Republic of China, develop children's physical and mental health, cultivate the foundation of national morality, and the basic knowledge and skills necessary for life, to cultivate citizens who know propriety, righteousness, love the country, and love the people." Further analysis of this overall goal is to "cultivate children's healthy physique, cultivate children's good character, develop children's aesthetic interests, enhance children's life knowledge and skills, train children's labor habits, inspire children's scientific thinking, cultivate children's spirit of mutual assistance and unity, and cultivate children's concept of loving the country and loving the community." Such educational goals are originally very relevant to the needs of today's national crisis environment. If we can truly follow these goals and achieve everything stipulated in those goals, so that today's children will become healthy citizens in the future, we will have already done the duty of education. Why do we need to come up with new tricks?

Furthermore, in terms of the goals of primary school citizenship training, the goal of our Chinese primary school citizenship training is to promote the inherent morality of the Chinese nation, with loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, righteousness, harmony, and peace as the center, and to adopt the virtues of other nations. Analyzed, it is to "cultivate habits of cleanliness and hygiene, a happy and lively spirit, concepts of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame, the virtue of fraternal sincerity, habits of thrift and labor, knowledge and skills of production and cooperation, concepts of public service and law-abiding, and thoughts of loving the country and loving the community." There is no doubt that such training goals are very relevant to the needs of today's national crisis environment. If we can truly follow this goal and achieve everything stipulated in that goal, so that today's children will become healthy citizens in the future, wouldn't we have done the duty of education? Originally, the Premier also said, "If we want to restore the status of the nation, in addition to everyone uniting to form a national group, we must restore the inherent morality. With inherent morality, then the inherent national status can be restored." Then, the goal of citizenship training that promotes the inherent morality of the nation and also adopts the virtues of other nations is, of course, the training goal of restoring national status. The so-called restoration of national status is to revive the nation, so that it can permanently exist independently in the world.

Based on everything mentioned above, we deeply feel that the purpose of Chinese education, whether viewed from the perspective of its purpose, goals, or any other aspect, is originally to seek national survival. Those who implement education, if they can truly and practically follow the purpose and goals, will naturally be able to achieve the goal of reviving the nation. Therefore, I personally believe that the more severe the national crisis, the more primary school educators should work hard. What they should work hard on is not to come up with new tricks, but to truly and practically follow the originally established educational purpose and goals and produce some practical effects. (End)

Shenbao Medical Journal

A Brief Introduction to Military Poison Gas

— Yao Xing-shu

The use of poison gas in warfare to deprive the enemy of combat and defensive capabilities has a long history. However, its concrete application began during the European War in 1914, when Germany pioneered its use. The average person harbors great fear of military poison gas. While we should not underestimate military poison gas, we must also break the blind fear, so that we can remain calm in an emergency, avoid panic, and calmly devise appropriate defensive plans to avoid most of the damage.

The name "military poison gas" is, in reality, somewhat inappropriate. Except for a few substances, not all of the materials used are gases. Some are liquids or solids with high boiling points, which are stored in bursting shells. When the shells explode, they turn into mist or dust and spread. Therefore, it is more reasonable to rename it as "chemical military supplies."

The purpose of using poison gas in wartime is, of course, to injure the enemy's body upon contact, depriving them of combat power and forcing them to withdraw from their guarded territory. The parts of the body that are harmed are nothing more than the mucous membranes of the eyes, nose, and throat, the lungs, and the skin.

Not all chemically toxic substances can be used as military poison gas. For example, carbon monoxide (the cause of coal briquette poisoning in winter), which is known for its severe toxicity, and hydrocyanic acid are not used militarily. To be used militarily, a substance must possess several physical and chemical properties.

I will now provide a general explanation of several important poison gases:

(1) Phosgene: Phosgene is the only toxic substance that is a gas at normal temperatures. It is colorless, has a distinctive odor, and cannot be stored for long in moist air. It is the most toxic and specifically attacks the lungs. It can easily cause death. When the air contains 45 milligrams of phosgene per cubic meter, it can be life-threatening. If 3.5 milligrams of this substance is inhaled within one second, death will occur immediately. Ordinary gas masks can protect against its attack because they contain reagents that absorb the substance. Spraying lime water can also quickly destroy it. This substance decomposes when affected by moisture (i.e., water) in the air, and its toxicity disappears.

(2) Diphosgene: Diphosgene is a colorless liquid at normal temperatures. When the pure product is heated to 120 degrees Celsius, it decomposes into phosgene. Its toxicity is equivalent to that of phosgene. It is stable and difficult to volatilize. It can remain on the ground for several hours without dissipating or changing. It has the same effect on the respiratory system as phosgene and is also a tear gas. Ordinary gas masks can prevent its attack. Spraying with lime water or calcium carbonate solution can completely destroy it.

(3) Chloropicrin: Chloropicrin is synthesized from bleaching powder and picric acid. It is a colorless, oily liquid that is insoluble in water and has a boiling point of 112 degrees Celsius. It is known as "vomiting gas" in the military. It is stable and can remain on the ground for a long time. Its vapor has a strong corrosive effect on the cornea and the mucous membranes of the nose and throat. When the air contains 19 milligrams of this substance per cubic meter, it causes tearing. At 60 milligrams, people cannot tolerate it, become dizzy, and vomit. Inhaling 16 milligrams within one minute will lead to immediate death. Its effectiveness is remarkable, and it is widely used. Spraying with liver of sulfur and soap solution can completely destroy it. It is quickly absorbed by activated carbon, so gas masks equipped with activated carbon can prevent its attack.

(4) Tear Gas (Chloracetophenone): Tear gas is a colorless crystalline solid that is insoluble in water and stable in nature. It dissolves in organic solvents and has an irritating effect on the eyes, causing tearing. However, recovery can occur after several minutes of inhaling fresh air. It is commonly used by the American police. Tightly fitting goggles can defend against it.

(5) Mustard Gas (Senfgas): This substance has a mustard-like odor, hence the name. It was widely used during the last European War. The pure product is a colorless liquid that is difficult to dissolve in water and can remain on the ground for several days. In winter, it can remain unchanged for months. It is a highly potent cellular toxin with great danger. When it is present in the air, people cannot detect it and do not experience noticeable pain. However, by the time the harm is detected, it is too late to provide aid. Extremely small amounts of mustard gas can cause obvious redness on the skin, gradually forming blisters, similar to burns. The speed and ease of recovery depend on the amount of toxin absorbed. It can also harm the lungs. Inhaling 12 milligrams within one minute can cause death. Gas masks are used to defend the respiratory organs. The rest of the body needs to be covered with clean and newly made rubber suits. Bleaching powder can destroy this substance. In cases of suspected mustard gas poisoning, bleaching powder solution can be used to wash the affected areas. Bleaching powder can be scattered on the ground or sprayed with its solution in areas full of mustard gas.

(6) Lewisite (Chlorovinylarsine): This substance has a scent similar to geraniums, also known as "death dew." It is a slightly yellow liquid that is difficult to dissolve in water but easily dissolves in organic solutions. It can cause blistering on the epidermis, like mustard gas. This substance was developed after the European War. The exact toxicity is unknown, but its irritating odor indicates its presence. It is also easily destroyed by alkaline solutions, cannot pass through gas filter kits, and its toxicity disappears upon contact with bleaching powder. Therefore, the effectiveness of its practical application remains to be proven.

(7) Diphenylarsine Chloride (Clark I): Diphenylarsine chloride is a solid with a high boiling point. It turns into a very fine mist when a gas shell explodes and flies around. It has a strong irritating effect on the nose, throat, and eyes. An concentration of 1 milligram per cubic meter of air is unbearable. This mist can penetrate ordinary respiratory filter kits, forcing the enemy to remove their gas masks. Taking this opportunity, a lung poison gas can be used to cause death. Adding a mist filter to the filter kit can defend against it. This substance decomposes and is destroyed upon contact with water.

(8) Diphenylarsine Cyanide (Clark II): Diphenylarsine Cyanide, readily degraded by water, led to the invention of this substance. It is also a solid, extremely difficult to dissolve in water, and durable. When the gas shell explodes, it turns into a fine mist that is a strong irritant to the mucous membranes of the eyes, nose, and throat. A concentration of 0.005 milligrams per cubic meter of air causes tearing, and at 0.25 milligrams, it is unbearable. This substance cannot penetrate mist filter kits.

In summary, of the military poison gases, phosgene, mustard gas, and Diphenylarsine cyanide are the three with intense danger. During the European War, a great number of different poison gases were used. It has been seventeen years since the end of the Great War, and who knows how many new inventions have been made. National defense chemistry is a closely guarded secret in every country, and we have no way of knowing the details. However, a method of protection can always be devised for each type of poison gas. Modern people cannot create a toxic substance that is absolutely impossible to defend against. Moreover, no matter what kind of poison gas it is, it is not easy to use it to kill all the residents of an entire city or town, because open space, wind, and rain are all natural defenses. However, in local warfare and the capture of fortresses, poison gas is indeed a threatening weapon.

Statistics on Child Mortality in Qimei Road Civilian Village, Shanghai

— Li Caihua

This is the result of a survey of 276 women in this village. To understand the number of child deaths, it is necessary to first describe the actual number of children born and the number of children currently living. Among the 276 women, two or three have never given birth. Some have been married for one to thirty years, and when asked why, they all answered with "I don't know." The 253 women who have given birth have collectively borne 994 children. Among them, 36 women gave birth to one child, accounting for 14.23%. Fifty-three women gave birth to two children, accounting for 20.95%. Forty-four women gave birth to three children, accounting for 17.39%. Twenty-seven women gave birth to four children, accounting for 10.67%. Thirty-five women gave birth to five children, accounting for 13.83%. Seventeen women gave birth to six children, accounting for 6.72%. Seventeen women gave birth to seven children, accounting for 6.72%. Twelve women gave birth to eight children, accounting for 4.74%. Five women gave birth to nine children, accounting for 1.98%. Four women gave birth to ten children, accounting for 1.58%. One woman gave birth to eleven children, accounting for 0.79%. Two women gave birth to twelve children, accounting for 0.79%. Women who gave birth to two children are the most numerous, while women who gave birth to eleven children are the least. On average, each woman gave birth to 3.53 children.

2.

The 253 women currently have 617 children, among which eleven women have no children. Women with one child are the most numerous, accounting for 28.09%. Followed by women with two children, accounting for 27.69%. Women with eight children are the least, accounting for 0.83%. The 242 women have an average of 2.54 children each. The 617 children account for 62.1% of the total number of children born.

3.

Out of the 994 children, a total of 377 died, accounting for 37.9% of the total number of children born. In terms of gender, the results are quite unexpected. We usually think that the concept of valuing boys over girls is firmly ingrained in the minds of the public, and that there must be more girls than boys who died. In reality, we only need to look at the age and cause of death statistics to understand. According to the author's survey, the gender distribution of child deaths is as follows: 200 males, accounting for 53.05%. This accounts for 20.12% of the total number of children born. 177 females, accounting for 46.95%. This accounts for 17.78% of the total number of children born. The percentage difference between males and females is 6.1%.

4.

As for the age at the time of child mortality, for clarity, it is listed in the table below:

Distribution of the common age of death of children of 253 women

In the table above, the group aged one to three years old has the highest number of deaths, followed by the group under half a month old, and the group aged thirteen to sixteen years old has the lowest number of deaths.

5.

Now let's talk about the causes of child mortality:

Sixty-two cases of tetanus, accounting for 16.45%. This accounts for 6.24% of the total number of children born.

Sixty-seven cases of measles, accounting for 17.77%. This accounts for 6.74% of the total number of children born.

Seventy-nine cases of meningitis, accounting for 20.95%. This accounts for 7.95% of the total number of children born.

Thirteen cases of diphtheria, accounting for 3.45%. This accounts for 1.31% of the total number of children born.

Thirty cases of smallpox, accounting for 7.96%. This accounts for 3.01% of the total number of children born.

Twenty-one cases of dysentery, accounting for 5.57%. This accounts for 2.11% of the total number of children born.

Ten cases of pneumonia, accounting for 2.65
