. This accounts for 1.01% of the total number of children born.

Twelve cases of pulmonary tuberculosis, accounting for 3.18%. This accounts for 1.21% of the total number of children born.

Thirty-three cases of typhoid fever, accounting for 8.73%. This accounts for 3.32% of the total number of children born.

Three cases of scarlet fever, accounting for 0.79%. This accounts for 0.30% of the total number of children born.

Three cases of whooping cough, accounting for 0.79%. This accounts for 0.30% of the total number of children born.

Five cases of cholera, accounting for 1.33%. This accounts for 0.50% of the total number of children born.

One case of appendicitis, accounting for 0.27%. This accounts for 0.11% of the total number of children born.

Eight cases of cerebral congestion, accounting for 2.12%. This accounts for 0.80% of the total number of children born.

Eight cases of pyemia, accounting for 2.12%. This accounts for 0.0%.

Four cases of bloating, accounting for 1.10%. This accounts for 0.40% of the total number of children born.

Nine cases of malnutrition, accounting for 2.38%. This accounts for 0.91% of the total number of children born.

Nine cases of accidental death, accounting for 2.38%. This accounts for 0.91% of the total number of children born.

6.

The above mortality figures are shocking, both in terms of age and cause of death. The most deaths are due to meningitis, followed by measles, then tetanus, and the least are due to appendicitis. In terms of age, as shown in the table above, the most are between one and three years old, followed by those under half a month old, and the fewest are between thirteen and sixteen years old. We know that the deaths under half a month old are all due to tetanus, and tetanus is the root of the problem caused by midwives. Midwives need to be trained, and this is imperative. As for midwives, the author surveyed 253 women who gave birth in this village, and it may be useful to tell the readers about this: 208 of the 253 women were delivered by midwives, accounting for 82.21%. Thirty-nine were delivered by Western doctors, accounting for 15.42%. Six were delivered by themselves, accounting for 2.37%.

Measles is originally a very easy-to-treat childhood disease and does not pose any danger. It can be dealt with as long as women have basic hygiene knowledge. However, the number of deaths due to measles accounts for the second largest number, which is shuddering to see. The immaturity of China's health education is very clear here.

The nine deaths due to poor nutrition, only one of them, due to the mother's illness and no milk to feed; the rest are because their mothers work all day and all night for livelihood, have no time to nurture, and starve their children to death alive. Labor crèches, labor crèches, please set them up universally! This is not only a medical problem, but also requires a great improvement in the entire society!

Medicinal Plants of Domestic Origin (Continued)

— Zhou Mengbai

Plantaginaceae

Plantain, *Plantago major* L. var. *asiatica* D.C.

(Plant) It grows wild in the mountains and fields and is a perennial herb. The leaves grow in clusters on a short stem, with long petioles, shaped like long ovals, with entire margins and several prominent leaf veins. Long stalks emerge from the leaf axils, bearing spicate inflorescences at the top. In summer, it blooms with small, pale purple, funnel-shaped flowers. The capsule is shaped like a small spindle.

(Crude Drug) Plantain Herb *Herba Plantaginis*, is the entire plant of plantain collected with flowers and dried.

Plantain Seed, *Semen Plantaginis*, is collected from its mature seeds. This product is not more than two millimeters in diameter, is a dark brown particle, and tastes slightly bitter. It is mucilaginous.

(Ingredients) The whole grass contains Aucubin C15H24O10 (glycoside). The seeds contain a large amount of mucilage, and other substances including Plantenolsaure C5H8O3 (?), succinic acid, Sfrnin, and Cholin. According to a report by Mr. Takahashi of Japan, the glycoside Plantagin was isolated from the whole grass.

(Pharmacology) According to Mr. Takahashi's experiments with Plantagin, it has a considerable effect on the respiratory center, making respiratory movements deep and slow, and has a significant antitussive effect. It can also excite the secretory nerves, increasing the mucus in the trachea and tracheal branches, and the secretion of digestive juices. However, it has no such effect on the dissolution of blood.

(Medicinal Use) Traditionally, plantain herb and plantain seed are considered diuretics. Plantain seed also has antitussive and antidiarrheal effects. The dosage is three to five grams, used in decoction.

Japanese Folklore: Plantain herb is said to be effective for treating stomach ailments when taken internally as a decoction. Plantain seed is said to be effective for treating eye ailments when taken internally as a decoction.

Orobanchaceae, *Boschniakia glabra*

(Plant) It grows wild in shady places under alpine trees and is an annual parasitic herb. It mostly parasitizes the roots of *Alnus alnobetula* Hart. var. *fruticosa* Winkl. The rhizome is lumpy. The stem is fleshy, cylindrical, usually about 30 cm tall. The leaves are scale-like, arranged like roof tiles, and are yellowish-brown. The top bears a spicate inflorescence, and in summer it blooms with purple-brown tubular flowers. The capsule is spherical.

(Crude Drug) *IIerba Boschniakiae*, is the entire plant collected and dried. The rhizome is lumpy, from which it is extracted. One or several stems, the stem is cylindrical, about 100 cm long, rarely reaching 30 cm, generally irregularly curved, and usually has an inflorescence. The surface of the stem is covered with scales, arranged like roof tiles, and is yellowish-brown or dark brown. The fracture surface is spongy. It has no significant odor.

(Medicinal Use) Traditionally, *Boschniakia glabra* is considered a tonic to strengthen the body and replenish essence.

The Importance of Summer Health Campaigns and Points to Note for Summer Health

— Hu Songshan

——A speech given on May 20th of the fifth year at the Summer Health Campaign Week in Yancheng County——

The four seasons of the year have different climates, and the diseases that occur also differ accordingly. In summer, the Fire Emperor unleashes his might, and the heat rises high, with the highest temperature of the year. At this time, the most severe, most dangerous, and deadly acute infectious diseases—"cholera," "typhoid fever," "dysentery," and other pathogenic bacteria—and the pathogenic protozoa of "malaria"—spores—emerge, thrive, and multiply. At the same time, the vectors of these infectious diseases, "flies" and "mosquitoes," also breed and multiply, acting as their slaves and lackeys, mediating transmission, assisting in evil, and aiding the wicked. They line up their troops, open up the battle lines, and launch an attack on our lives. This time can be said to be the weather when we are most susceptible to infectious diseases, and it can be said to be the season when we are most prone to death. If we are even slightly careless in our diet, daily life, and all aspects of daily living, and do not pay attention to hygiene, then we will have the opportunity to contract diseases and risk our lives. If we ourselves or someone else does not pay attention to hygiene and contracts an acute infectious disease—"cholera," "typhoid fever," "dysentery," or "malaria"—it will not simply end there. It will also infect others! Therefore, often once a transmission starts, it spreads in all directions, rampages rampant, harms society, deaths are everywhere, and it is unstoppable, as the saying goes, "A spark can start a prairie fire, spreading inexhaustibly." In addition, there is also "heatstroke," which is also a summer disease and is also very dangerous, with the risk of death. The so-called "heatstroke" includes two types of illnesses, one called "heat exhaustion" and the other called "sunstroke." What is called "heat exhaustion"? In weather with extremely high temperatures and saturated air, feeling extremely depressed and having difficulty breathing, resulting in sudden mental confusion and unconsciousness, this is called "heat exhaustion." What is called "sunstroke"? In weather with extremely high temperatures, extremely low humidity, and strong sunlight, being directly exposed to sunlight and becoming mentally confused and unconscious, this is called "sunstroke." This is what is commonly called heatstroke, which is also very dangerous.

According to statistics from the Ministry of Health, the number of unnatural deaths in our country is as high as six million each year, compared to other countries, and the majority of these six million deaths are due to epidemics. Why is the mortality rate in our country so high? Upon investigation, it goes without saying that it is naturally because the public lacks knowledge and does not pay attention to hygiene, leading to this result. In particular, the failure to pay attention to summer hygiene is the biggest reason. Since summer hygiene is so important, but the general public is so unattentive, what should be done? It is necessary to use this kind of grand and enthusiastic campaign week to promote awareness and arouse national public attention to summer hygiene in particular, in order to protect individual lives, the lives of the masses, and the health of the nation. Otherwise, without engaging in campaigns to attract attention, and the general public still being so inattentive, then during this summer, the lives of individuals, the lives of the masses, and the health of the nation will have no guarantee. Especially this summer, extra attention must be paid. Why? Based on history and experience, we know that there is a major flood every ten years and a minor flood every five years. This year is the year of a minor flood. We also know that epidemics often accompany floods. According to general speculation, this year is also a year of cholera epidemics, so extra attention is needed.

Illness, death, economic losses, population losses, national losses, and ethnic losses are all immeasurable. How terrible and heartbreaking this is! From this perspective, how important is the summer health campaign? Can we neglect it? Can we casually and carelessly not make efforts?

As for the points to note for summer health, the following is a report:

Pay attention to drinking water. Unclean water sources should not be used. Unboiled water should not be drunk.

Pay attention to food. 1. Do not eat old, rotten, fly-infested, or leftover food.

2. Do not eat melons and fruits that have been soaked in raw water or cut open for some time.

3. Do not eat unclean melons, fruits, ice cream, and other foods on street stalls and in stores.

4. Food must be covered with gauze to prevent flies from contacting and leaving germs on it.

5. Do not eat too much, to avoid indigestion. Food staying in the stomach and intestines for too long will rot and decompose, which is a cause of disease.

Avoid eating raw food. Eating raw food is also a cause of disease in summer. Often someone eats raw food in the morning and gets sick in the evening, so it should be avoided.

Eliminate mosquitoes. Mosquitoes are vectors for transmitting malaria, which is very serious. The first excavation of the Panama Canal failed because they harmed the workers, which is ironclad proof. Their larvae are called mosquito larvae, which live in sewage. The elimination method is to drain the sewage in gutters and pits, not allowing it to accumulate, so that the mosquito larvae have no place to survive. Sewage must also be disinfected with formalin or Lysol solution. Mosquitoes must also be eliminated urgently.

Eliminate flies. Flies are vectors for transmitting cholera, typhoid fever, and dysentery. Their larvae are called maggots, which live in manure pits. The elimination method is to pour lime milk or carbolic acid water into the manure pit, which can eliminate them completely. For flies, use flypaper, fly swatters, or fly traps to eliminate them.

Avoid being bitten by mosquitoes. Doors and windows must be fitted with screen doors and windows, and mosquito nets must be hung on beds; they must be tightly pressed around the edges to avoid being bitten by mosquitoes, which can lead to malaria.

Pay attention to cleanliness and disinfection. All daily necessities and clothing, etc., must be thoroughly cleaned and disinfected to prevent germs from parasitizing and transmitting diseases. Cleaning means washing frequently. Disinfection can be done by boiling, which is the most convenient, economical, and complete.

Avoid heatstroke. Avoid heatstroke to prevent heatstroke and other causes of acute infectious diseases.

Avoid moving under the hot sun. Walking or working under the hot sun should be avoided to prevent sunstroke.

Avoid sleeping outdoors. Sleeping outdoors on summer nights makes it easy to catch a cold and is a cause of various diseases, so it should be avoided.

In short, we should pay special attention to improving anything that is unhygienic. The above points seem very ordinary, but they are very important. If we follow them, we can naturally avoid diseases.

Common Knowledge Q&A about Teeth (33)

— Lin Jianxian

(Question 160) Can dental diseases be treated by self-treatment?

Answer: The treatment and repair of dental diseases mostly falls within the scope of dentists. The purpose of this chapter is only to give indications of what patients want to know and should know. Its purpose is to make patients feel the necessity of early treatment when encountering dental diseases, so as to avoid delays; during the treatment period, to know a little about the general procedures of treatment, so as not to often harbor doubts or distrust, hindering the progress of treatment; to be able to cooperate with the dentist and implement the various items he has instructed at home, so as to promote the effectiveness of treatment; if a dentist's diagnosis and treatment cannot be obtained temporarily, to be able to know something about what can be done by oneself to cope with emergencies.

Section 2 Treatment of Dental Caries and Pulp Diseases

(Question 161) How should small cavities that are just beginning be treated?

Answer: You should ask a dentist to first use a dental drill to remove the decayed part of the cavity, then disinfect it with medicine, and then fill it with durable materials. The smaller the cavity, the easier it is to repair, and the better the effect.

(Question 162) How should cavities that already feel painful be treated?

Answer: First, the decayed part should be drilled away, and only after the pain has been cured can it be filled.

(Question 163) After sealing pain-relieving medicine, if the pain is still severe, how should it be treated?

Answer: At this time, the cavity is already deep, and the pulp has become inflamed and painful and cannot be preserved. The pulp should be removed first, and then filled, commonly called nerve extraction.

(Question 164) What is the procedure for extracting the pulp?

Answer: When the pulp is alive, it is unbearably painful to the touch, so it must be killed or anesthetized with medicine before it can be removed. Anesthesia with medicine allows for extraction at that time, while sealing medicine to kill it requires one or two days. When extracting, drill open the pulp chamber and use a very thin, barbed long needle to extract all the pulp in the root canals.

(Question 165) Why must patients strictly abide by the dentist's instructions after the medicine to kill the pulp is sealed?

Answer: The medicine to kill the pulp is very strong, and patients must go back for a follow-up visit at the time agreed upon by the dentist, and must not be overdue, so as to avoid causing apical periodontitis. If you feel that the sealed medicine has fallen out or seeped out halfway, you should immediately inform the dentist.

(Question 166) After the pulp is extracted, what is the filling procedure?

Answer: After the pulp is extracted, for the sake of stability, it is necessary to rest for a week or ten days. If it goes well, then filling can be done. When filling, fill the root canals first, and then rest for two or three days. If there are no abnormalities, the remaining part can be filled. Therefore, the time and surgery required to treat teeth with extracted pulp are three or four times more than those for treating simple cavities. Therefore, the surgical fees charged by dentists are probably about three times higher.

(Question 167) After the root canal is filled, what symptoms may occur?

Answer: Because the filling material in the root canal stimulates the apical periodontium, mild apical periodontitis may occur sometimes, and the teeth may feel slightly floating and uncomfortable, but it can recover after a few days. If the pain continues unabated, the filling material should be removed, and it should be refilled after it has been cured.

(Question 168) How should teeth with decayed pulp be treated?

Answer: If the pulp has already rotted, it will produce a peculiar stench. The root canal should be opened first, and the decayed material should be washed away. Disinfecting medicine should be sealed, and it should be replaced daily or every other day until the cavity has no odor, then it can be filled. Therefore, the procedure is very troublesome. If the apical periodontium is involved, it should be treated according to the treatment method for apical periodontitis in the next section.

(Question 169) How should cavities in baby teeth be treated?

Answer: If baby teeth develop cavities before the time for tooth replacement, you should immediately ask a doctor to fill them, and do not delay, so as to avoid decay and early loss.

(Question 170) Why should teeth that are decayed and cannot be filled, or decayed tooth roots, be extracted early?

Answer: These residual teeth have lost their chewing function. If they are allowed to remain, there is a risk of causing acute infectious apical periodontitis. On the one hand, it is a major base for the accumulation of bacteria and dirt in the mouth. On the other hand, because the residual pulp rots and becomes purulent inside, it is an entry point for pus to enter the human body. Therefore, this source of trouble should be removed as soon as possible.

Common Knowledge Q&A about Diseases

— Cheng Hancao

(84) Trichinosis

What kind of disease is trichinosis?

This is a disease in which worms parasitize the intestines and muscles of animals.

Who discovered trichinosis?

It was discovered by Mr. Zenker. The Western name is Trichinella spiralis.

Which animals did this worm originally parasitize in?

Most of them parasitize in pigs, and sometimes they also parasitize in white mice, gray mice, rabbits, and dogs. Among them, intestinal trichinella and muscle trichinella can be distinguished.

How do trichinella that parasitize in the human body invade?

Because the larvae of trichinella often exist in pig muscles, people are invaded into the stomach if they eat undercooked pork; then the envelope of the larvae falls off and becomes intestinal trichinella. The mother worms of this intestinal trichinella parasitize in the intestinal wall, and the larvae enter the muscles through the lymphatic vessels and blood vessels, becoming spiral, wrapped in a calcareous envelope. When observed with the naked eye, there are many grayish-white spots in the meat, which are these larvae.

What are the symptoms when suffering from trichinosis?

After infection, there must be an incubation period of three or four days before the disease occurs. The symptoms of the disease can be divided into two stages.

What are the symptoms in the first stage?

In the first stage, there is pressure in the stomach, nausea, vomiting, abdominal pain, diarrhea, and sometimes constipation. At the same time, there is muscle pain and muscle rigidity. Accompanied by chills, shivering, and fever, and the face, especially the eyelids, becomes swollen. Such symptoms last for a week before entering the second stage.

What are the symptoms in the second stage?

When it reaches the second stage, the trichinella larvae in the blood enter the muscles, so the affected muscles are swollen and painful, and reflexes are reduced or disappear. If it invades the masticatory muscles, pharyngeal muscles, and throat and eye muscles, there will be difficulty in chewing or swallowing, hoarseness, and eye pain; especially importantly, if it invades the respiratory muscles, diaphragm muscles, and intercostal muscles, there will be chest pain, insufficient breathing, and difficulty in breathing, and even bronchial pneumonia due to the accumulation of sputum. During this second stage, the trunk and limbs often develop swelling, chills, shivering, and fever persist, or there may be headache, insomnia, confusion, and splenomegaly and meningitis symptoms.

What are the abnormalities in the skin, blood, and urine of patients with trichinosis?

The skin develops creeping rash, urticaria, small hemorrhages, pustular rash, or miliaria. White blood cells increase in the blood, and protein is found in the urine.

What is the prognosis of this disease?

Mild cases are cured in two or three weeks; severe and chronic cases take seven or eight weeks. Thirty to forty out of a hundred people do not recover.

How to treat and prevent?

In the early stage, use strong laxatives to try to eliminate the parasitic worms. When there is muscle pain, use chloroform to rub, apply warm damp cloths locally, bathe, or inject morphine, etc. The method of prevention is to not eat undercooked pork.

The order was misplaced by the printer, and is hereby corrected.

Special Telegraphic Supplement

Brief Account of the Method for Collect Telegrams in China

— Zhen

The method of collect telegrams has been implemented for international telegrams and domestic news telegrams for many years, providing general convenience. However, ordinary telegrams used by the domestic public have not been opened, so the business has not developed. In order to facilitate domestic public communication, the Ministry of Communications promulgated "Fifteen Articles on the Method of Collect Telegrams in China" on May 27th of this year, which came into effect on June 1st. A brief description of the key procedures is provided below:

Procedures for the Sender's Request

When making a request, the sender should obtain a blank application form from the local telegraph office and fill in the following items: Name, occupation, and detailed address of the applicant (if there is a telegraphic registration number, please indicate it); Place of origin of the telegram; Name and detailed address of the recipient (if there is a telegraphic registration number, please indicate it); Type of telegram to be sent, etc. Submit it to the telegraph office for submission to the Telegraph Administration of the Ministry of Communications for approval. After receiving the application, the Telegraph Administration will instruct the receiving telegraph office to contact the recipient for agreement, fill out the "Voluntary Application for Payment of Domestic Collect Telegrams," sign and seal it, and prepay a deposit sufficient for half a month's telegram fees to the receiving telegraph office. The office will then submit it to the Telegraph Administration, which will instruct the sending telegraph office to notify the sender to begin sending telegrams.

Procedures for the Recipient's Request

If the request is made by the recipient, a written statement should be made to the local telegraph office, stating that the recipient will be responsible for the telegram fees for certain types of telegrams sent by a specific person from a specific location in China. With the consent of the local telegraph office, the recipient will fill out the "Voluntary Application for Payment of Domestic Collect Telegram Fees," sign and seal it, and pay a deposit. The office will then submit it to the Telegraph Administration for investigation by the sending office and to notify the sender to complete the application and begin sending telegrams.

Procedures for Sending Telegrams

The telegraph office will provide the sender with a telegram receipt book. When sending a telegram, the receiving staff of the telegraph office will sign the book as proof of receipt, without issuing a receipt. However, the sender should submit a sample of their seal or signature to the telegraph office for verification. When sending a telegram, the sender should affix their seal or signature at the bottom of the telegram paper for verification.

Procedures for Settling Telegram Fees

The receiving telegraph office will prepare a monthly statement based on the telegrams received and settle the telegram fees with the recipient. After receiving the statement, the recipient must pay the fees within five days at the latest. If the fees are not paid by the sixth month, the receiving telegraph office will collect the telegram fees from the recipient one by one before delivering the telegrams. If the fees are still not paid after another five days, the receiving office will deduct the fees from the deposit. If the deposit is insufficient, the remaining amount will still be pursued. At the same time, an official telegram will be sent to the Telegraph Administration to notify the sending office to revoke the sender's right to send telegrams in accordance with this method.

Advantages of This Method

The business operations of major commercial firms often rely on their branches in various locations to promote sales. The quantity of sales and the business situation in various locations must be reported to the head office by telegram every day in order to plan for expansion or contraction. This type of commercial firm telegram is best suited for using the "Collect Telegram Method," because all the telegram fees sent by the branches are paid by the head office. This gives the head office the right to control communications, while the branches are only responsible for sending telegrams, which is convenient for both parties. Furthermore, the telegram receiving procedure relies on signatures in the receipt book without issuing receipts, which eliminates the need to calculate telegram fees on the spot, significantly increasing speed.

Talking About Chinese Telegraph Machines Invented by Chinese People

— Hua

We all know that Chinese telegraphy uses numbers to replace characters, which is an indirect way of transmission. Although this indirect transmission method has various shortcomings, Chinese characters are not like foreign words that are pieced together letter by letter. Its extensive and complex vocabulary cannot be transmitted by current telegraph machines. Therefore, some enthusiasts of the national phonetic movement have been advocating the use of phonetic symbols to replace the current four-code telegraph, but the following difficulties have also arisen: The social application of phonetic symbols has not yet reached the point of widespread use, and most of the public still use the original characters to send telegrams. The phonetic symbol alphabet has many letters, which is not suitable for the transmission of new-style sending and receiving machines. Phonetic symbols have difficulties with the four tones and homophones. Receiving a telegram that is entirely in phonetic symbols still requires guesswork. Therefore, using phonetic symbols to transmit Chinese telegrams still cannot solve the difficulty of directly transmitting characters. In this article, I will introduce Chinese telegraph machines that have been invented by Chinese people in recent years that can directly transmit Chinese characters. Although these machines have not yet been used in telegraph offices, they are theoretically flawless and will soon be approved by the authorities and adopted by telegraph offices across the country.

As far as I know, there are currently two types of Chinese telegraph machines that have been successfully invented: those designed by Mr. Cen Shilong and Mr. Wang Bonian. I will briefly introduce the principles of these two telegraph machines to readers.

Cen's Chinese Telegraph Machine: The principle behind this type of telegraph machine is as follows: It arranges 10,000 commonly used Chinese characters according to the layout of coordinate paper, with ten rows and ten columns vertically and horizontally. Each grid has ten lines. The horizontal grid represents the thousands place, the horizontal row represents the hundreds place, the vertical grid represents the tens place, and the vertical row represents the ones place. The position of each character is arranged according to the above-mentioned thousands, hundreds, tens, and ones places of the military code number. For example, if the code for the character "电" (dian, electricity) is "7193," then the position of the character should be in the eighth horizontal grid (from right to left), the second row, the tenth grid downward, and the fourth character. (Note: Because the first grid and the first row are both zero positions, one must be added.) Chinese characters arranged in this way are made into inverted type wheels using a lightweight chemical alloy. The movement of the type wheels is controlled by a horizontal feed and a vertical feed gear. The action of the gears is controlled by the current sent by the other party. Direct transmission of Chinese telegraphs is thus completed. Mr. Cen Shilong has spared no effort in researching Chinese telegraph machines. After inventing this method of transmitting Chinese telegrams, he went a step further and designed an automatic telegraph machine to transmit Chinese telegrams, so as not to affect the original speed of the telegraph. This machine has not yet been publicly tested because its structure is more complicated. With Mr. Cen's perseverance and talent, I think the government will definitely have ways to encourage him to successfully manufacture the machine and put it into practical use as soon as possible.

Wang's Chinese Telegraph Machine: Mr. Wang's invented Chinese telegraph machine has three types: A, B, and C. The Type A Chinese telegraph machine is suitable for use with Morse machines and wireless telegraph earphones currently used in China. The machine is equipped with a character disk, with 100 lines and 100 characters in each line, totaling 10,000 characters. The disk is equipped with a handle that can be moved at will. Next to the handle is a pointer. When sending a telegram, move the pointer to any character in the disk and press down. The corresponding code for that character will be automatically sent to the circuit. A common Chinese typewriter is installed in the receiving telegraph office. The characters in the disk are replaced with numbers. When the receiving operator receives the number code, they align it with the number in the disk and press down. The Chinese typewriter can then type out the corresponding character. The Type B Chinese telegraph machine is suitable for Weishi and Keli automatic machines currently used in China. The structure and usage method of this machine are exactly the same as Type A, but it needs to be equipped with a Keli keyboard perforator. When sending a telegram, move the pointer on the character disk to any character in the disk and press down. The corresponding code for that character will be automatically punched on the oiled paper strip by the keyboard perforator. The punched oiled paper strip is then sent out using the Weishi automatic sending machine. On the receiving side, the Keli receiving and re-punching machine receives it. The oiled paper strip received by the Keli receiving and re-punching machine is then placed in the Type C Chinese telegraph machine, which automatically prints out the characters.

Mr. Wang's invented Chinese telegraph machine has been successfully manufactured. It is said that the Ministry of Communications has specially approved Mr. Wang to go to Beijing for a public test. I hope to have better news to report to readers in the next issue of this publication.

Points to Note for Gentlemen Sending Telegrams

Gentlemen sending telegrams, if you pay attention to the following points when sending telegrams, you will definitely be able to improve the telegraph speed invisibly!

Add the original characters to self-translated codes: It is inevitable that there will be errors in self-translation of codes when you are busy! If you add the original characters next to the code, then the telegraph office will have the opportunity to proofread your telegram after receiving it. If there is a mistranslation, they can correct it for you immediately.

Write telegrams clearly: If the writing in the telegram is scribbled, it is easy for the telegraph office staff to misread the words when they are busy, resulting in errors. For example, in English telegrams, cursive lowercase A and OO, ON and UE, LB and F, etc., are prone to errors due to unclear writing. If a clarification is required, it will inevitably delay the time. If no clarification is sought, the error will occur! As for Chinese telegraph characters, all simplified characters and cursive characters are bound to cause errors, affecting the effectiveness of the telegram. Therefore, regardless of whether it is a Chinese or English telegram, it is best to write the telegram clearly in regular script so that it is easy to understand at a glance, guaranteeing that there will be no errors!

Write the recipient's name and address in detail: In the past, in order to save money, senders often shortened the recipient's name and address as much as possible, resulting in many cases of "improper delivery," "time-consuming delivery," or "misdelivery." Now, for Chinese telegrams, the sender's name and address within thirteen characters are charged as three characters, so you don't have to reduce the number of characters as before, which may lead to misdelivery.

Write the sender's own name and address at the bottom of the telegram: If the sender's name and address are written in detail at the bottom of the telegram, then if there is any "undeliverable" or other situation with the telegram, the telegraph office can notify you according to the name and address written. If the name and address are not indicated at the bottom of the telegram, it will be impossible to notify you, which may delay your important business!

A Historical Observation of Telegraph Administration Organization

Since the Republic of China, the telegraph administration organization in China can be divided into four periods: the first period was the era of the Beijing government, the second period was the early era of the National Government, the third period was the recent era, and the fourth period is the future era. These are described separately below: In the era of the Beijing government, wireless telegraph stations and telephone bureaus were directly under the ministry, while long-distance telephones were handled concurrently by the telephone bureaus. Due to the particularly heavy workload of wired telegraphs, they were managed by region. Regional management agencies were established between the Ministry of Communications and the various telegraph bureaus. The names of these management agencies changed from time to time, and the regional divisions were also increased or decreased, but the nature of their transit functions remained unchanged. The telegraph administration organization during this period was mainly based on wired telegraphs.

After the establishment of the National Government, the organization of wired telegraphs and local telephones remained the same. However, with the rapid development of wireless telegraphs and long-distance telephones, the "Wireless Telegraph and Telephone Management Office" was established to manage all wireless telegraph stations in the country. The "Long-Distance Telephone Traffic Management Office" was established to manage long-distance telephone affairs across the country by region. Later, the "Wireless Telegraph and Telephone Management Office" was reorganized into the "International Telecommunications Bureau," with the two main functions of handling international communications and domestic wireless communications. The "Long-Distance Telephone Traffic Management Office" was originally divided by line, but later it was reorganized into the "Long-Distance Telephone Management Office," with the provincial area as the division standard. At this time, the telegraph administration organization in China was divided into four major systems: wired telegraphs, wireless telegraphs, local telephones, and long-distance telephones.

In the past two or three years, the Ministry of Communications has felt that the telegraph administration organization was inevitably scattered. In order to centralize power and save expenses, it has vigorously sought reforms. The first thing that has been implemented is the merger of bureaus and stations, merging the various wireless telegraph stations and wired telegraph bureaus to establish local telegraph offices. Where there are no local telegraph offices, they are subject to the command of the regional telegraph administration bureau due to factual relations. The second is the merger of telegraph and telephone bureaus. All ministry-run telephone bureaus across the country, except for a few bureaus with larger projects and particularly heavy workloads, are merged with local telegraph bureaus to establish telegraph bureaus. The third is the merger of wired telegraphs and long-distance telephones, abolishing the "Long-Distance Telephone Management Office" and transferring the management rights of long-distance telephones in each province and region to the Telegraph Administration Bureau. The long-distance telephone business organizations are also merged with the telegraph departments to establish jointly. At this time, the telegraph administration organization in China has merged wired telegraphs, wireless telegraphs, local telephones, and long-distance telephones into a unified system.

Since telegraph and telephone services have been merged and managed, a complete set of organizational rules is needed to comply with them. The Ministry of Communications promulgated the "Organizational Rules of the Telegraph Administration Bureau" on May 13th, and ordered the whole country to implement them from June 1st. The Administration Bureau is divided into four sections: General Affairs, Telegraph Affairs, Telephone Affairs, and Engineering Affairs, and one accounting office. The Telegraph Affairs section is divided into Wired, Wireless, and Business sections, which are responsible for the wired telegraph service, wireless telegraph service, and wired and wireless telegraph business matters in the entire region, respectively. The Telephone Affairs section is divided into Local, Long-Distance, and Business sections, which are responsible for the local telephone, long-distance telephone traffic, and local and long-distance telephone business matters in the entire region, respectively. The Engineering Affairs section is divided into Machinery Lines, and Materials sections, which are responsible for telecommunications machinery, telecommunications lines, and telecommunications materials in the entire region, respectively. However, in areas where there are no local or long-distance telephones, or where there are established but the business is simple, no telephone affairs section is established, and its responsibilities are merged into the telegraph affairs section. If the affairs of the section are simple, the number of divisions may be reduced. The purpose of the future telegraph administration organization is to implement a unified plan for the overall situation on the one hand, and to achieve the effect of adapting to local conditions on the other hand, aiming to concentrate power, save expenses, and increase office efficiency.

Looking at the changes in the telegraph administration organization since the Republic of China, it has changed from simple to complex, and then from complex to simple. The reason for changing from simple to complex is to seek the rapid development of new businesses, while the reason for changing from complex to simple is to focus on rational management. Although the trends are different, the effects are initially the same.

Q&A Column

This publication has specially opened a Q&A column. Social figures are welcome to ask about telephone sending and receiving procedures, unclear points in telecommunications regulations, or any telecommunications knowledge they wish to inquire about. This publication will provide a detailed answer.

Mr. Zhang Zengxiang from Nanchang asks:

Which coastal radio stations in China and abroad provide sending and receiving services for ship telegrams? Which ones do not? In particular, I am most eager to know about those in China.

(Answer) There are a total of five coastal radio stations in China: Shanghai, Qingdao, Fuzhou, Tianjin, and Yantai. There is one in Hankou, which will be opened soon.

Is there a fixed regulation for which coastal radio station should transmit ship telegrams for ships in a certain area? (For example, if a ship is traveling between Hankou and Anhui, which station should be responsible for relaying it?)

(Answer) When sending ship telegrams, you should first estimate the distance the ship is currently traveling. If the ship is traveling between Hankou and Anhui, it should be relayed by the Shanghai radio station. When the Hankou radio station is established in the future, it will be relayed by Hankou. If the ship is in the Bohai Sea, it should be relayed by the Yantai radio station.

According to the examples given in the rules for Chinese and English formats, such as "(Official Cabin No. 10, Wang Liangji, Sinming, Qingdao)" and "(Nelson SS Sinming Tsingtaoradio)," should SS also be added before Sinming in Chinese? Should (Radio) also be added after Qingdao? Should Sinming be written as two characters or one character? Should Qingdao be written as two characters or one character? (Is Radio written as a separate word? Or is it attached to the place name and not counted as a word? Please provide details. How many words should (Tsingtaoradio) be counted as?

(Answer) It is not necessary to add SS before Sinming in Chinese. It is also not necessary to add (Radic) after Qingdao. Sinming and Qingdao are both counted as two characters for billing. (Tsingtaoradio) in English is counted as one word for billing.

Chunqiu

Snippets

— (Rongyu)

In the past, there was a traveler who saw three old men in the field, each over a hundred years old, working together to weed the crops. He got out of his carriage and asked the three old men how they had achieved such longevity. The eldest old man stepped forward and said, "I sleep at night without covering my head." The middle old man stepped forward and said, "My wife is ugly." The youngest old man stepped forward and said, "I eat sparingly, according to my appetite." How meaningful are the words of the three old men! That is why they can live so long.

This is a poem called "Three Old Men" written by Mr. Ying Zhen of the Jin Dynasty. Although it is an old antique, it coincides with modern hygiene methods. If you try it according to the prescription, it will be more effective than getting a "Vitamin C Life-Saving" shot! Because "breathing fresh air," "moderation in sexual desire," and "careful eating" are all known to be important, but few people can put them into practice. Especially people in the city, who spend all night partying and indulging in wine and food, are bound to compromise their health. After reading this poem, do you not have any warning?

Remembering "Old Buddha Chen"

— Qingqu

The person "Old Buddha Chen" is worth commemorating because in the fifth and sixth days of May in the twenty-second year of Daoguang in the Former Qing Dynasty, many British warships dared to sail into the Wusongkou. Seeing the fluttering flags blocking the sea, "Old Buddha Chen," who was originally the Jiangnan Admiral and was transferred to defend Wusong only ten days earlier, naturally could not surrender when the enemy approached the city, as it would violate the orders of his superiors. Therefore, "Old Buddha Chen" immediately led his subordinates, day and night, to set up a death camp along the coast to fight a desperate battle with the enemy.

At that time, "Old Buddha Chen" was very strict in governing the army. At the moment of mobilization, he issued a military order: "Anyone who takes a bundle of firewood or grass from the people... will be beheaded." Therefore, his army could be said to be impeccable. Unexpectedly, the camp was barely set up. In less than a day, British warships had already approached and opened fire first, attacking our western battery. "Old Buddha Chen" directed the battle for two hours and drove back the British warships. Unfortunately, Governor Niu Jian, stationed in Baoshan City, heard the news of the victory and wanted to share the credit. Unexpectedly, he rode in a sedan chair, followed by hundreds of soldiers, and was spotted by British soldiers as soon as he arrived at Shanghai Tang. They fired a cannon, and the exploding shell landed right in front of Niu Jian's sedan chair, almost scaring him out of his wits. He hurriedly retreated. The enemy knew that there were no reinforcements, and tried their best to attack our battery again. "Old Buddha Chen" resisted with his isolated army, refusing to yield. Hey! Suddenly, Xu Zhou Commander Wang Zhiyuan came to "Old Buddha Chen" and suggested surrender. "Old Buddha Chen" was furious, and Zhiyuan fled with Niu Jian. "Old Buddha Chen" stood still, fighting his way through a hail of bullets. In the end, he was wounded in the left flank and fell to the ground. However, he still struggled to get up, still waving the flag with his right hand, shouting not to retreat and encouraging his soldiers. Later, he died in battle due to his serious injuries, and Wusong, a strategic stronghold in the southeast, was lost.

"Old Buddha Chen's" body was later carried by soldier Liu Guobiao and hidden in the reeds outside the east gate of Baoshan. After seven days, it had not yet been collected. Chen Tinghuang, the magistrate of Jiading, went and wept over the body and took care of the funeral. In the early days of the Opium War, the Qing court received a report and posthumously named "Old Buddha Chen" the Duke of Zhongmin and established a special ancestral hall in Baoshan City (now the County Junior High School). The portrait of "Old Buddha Chen" is still preserved to this day, and his memorial day is on May 8th. His name was "Huacheng," his style name was "Lianfeng," and he was from Tongan County, Fujian. In his youth, he could walk underwater and swim hundreds of miles. The people of Jia and Bao called him "Old Buddha Chen" because he shared weal and woe with the soldiers and was able to defend the coast and protect our local area.

Bare Arms and Legs

— Wei Jing

Since women gained liberation, their arms have also been liberated. The sleeves of cheongsams have gradually retreated from the wrists to the elbow, and even further to an inch or two from the shoulders. The sleeves have already retreated as far as they can go, so people's eyes naturally move downwards to the legs. The trouser legs, originally reaching the ankles, have been shortened to the knees, and even further to seven or eight inches above the knees. Thus, when summer comes, women's cheongsams are almost like vests on the upper body, and even with the high slits of the cheongsams, the trouser legs are barely visible. Both jade arms and jade legs are completely exposed.

Every year, children need to be vaccinated against smallpox to avoid the danger of contracting it. When short-sleeved cheongsams first became popular, mothers generally vaccinated their young daughters on their legs instead of their arms, saying that the cheongsam sleeves were getting shorter day by day, and it would be unsightly if large smallpox scars were visible on their arms. At that time, I greatly admired their thoughtfulness. Later, the cheongsam sleeves really did shrink to the shoulders, and I admired their foresight even more. But times are constantly evolving, and now the trouser legs are also gone. I wonder what the mothers who were so thoughtful for their daughters in the past will do. I also wonder where the mothers who are vaccinating their daughters today will inoculate them to ensure complete safety.

In the past, because women didn't wear socks in the summer, the sock factory owners appealed for a strict ban on bare feet. But now, bare arms and legs are prevalent, and I think the fabric store owners may also make an appeal in the future. However, here, I want to sincerely appeal to the modern-loving women to expose their esteemed arms and legs less if possible, because the motive for exposing arms and legs is only to show their healthy beauty. The legs and arms of our country's women, who lack exercise, are mostly either too thin or too fat, and there is nothing to see. Some are even covered with bedbug bites and frostbite scars, which really make people not dare to admire them.

The Phoenixes Change Nests

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 4: Fine Rain and Slanting Wind Still Leave Traces; Quiet Night, a Person Writes a Letter of Severance

Dreams are the hub of nervous sensations. Because the blood vessels concentrate blood flow, illusions and hallucinations are produced. Blood flow is not really a mysterious thing. However, dreamers always suspect that there is a premonition within it, and the more thoughtful a person is, the more likely they are to dream, and the more they treat dreams as a premonition. The dream that Jiang Menglan had that night struck his heart because the thing he couldn't get in reality, he got in the dream. Many people cannot satisfy their desires and rely entirely on dreaming to satisfy them. However, after that moment of satisfaction, it often increases their sadness and indignation. Menglan didn't turn on the light, and stood in the dark room like that. He didn't sigh softly until he heard two distant rooster crows. He went to bed to rest. He woke up a little late the next morning, hurriedly washed his face, and quickly took his schoolbag and went to school. As he walked on the road, he thought to himself that he wouldn't encounter Zhang Guoqi today. The time they usually met on the road had passed. This thought was not like in the past, when he would look ahead early on. This time, he lowered his head and walked step by step. When he walked into that narrow alley, he heard a burst of footsteps. He looked up and couldn't help but take a step back. It was the very person he was thinking of. After their meeting at Yuhua Terrace yesterday, they felt very familiar with each other. It seemed too impolite to just look at each other like this. Therefore, in that intentional or unintentional moment, a shallow smile appeared on his face. It could be said that this smile was not for Zhang Guoqi, because he didn't look directly at Zhang Guoqi. But could it be said that he wasn't smiling at Guoqi? However, there was no one else in this narrow alley. Therefore, although Guoqi couldn't immediately express his gratitude, he deeply understood this gentle and bright smile. Moreover, as they passed each other, it was inconvenient to stop. The time when their eyes met was very short. Even if Guoqi wanted to return the greeting, it was too late. Fortunately, two hours later, when they returned from school, Guoqi would have a way to repay the shallow smile he had received. In order to respond to this shallow smile, he quickly ran towards this alley from school. When he arrived at the entrance of the alley, he didn't see Jiang Menglan, so he didn't dare to walk too fast. Because if he walked too fast and passed two or three alleys, they would separate and wouldn't be able to meet. He walked so slowly, each foot pausing for a minute before moving forward. (35)

After Reading the Observation Notes on Famous Chinese Paintings

— Ma Gongyu

My friend Shi Jun, who is skilled in calligraphy and good at painting, is devoted to writing. He has seen many famous paintings. Recently, he wrote "Observation Notes on Famous Chinese Paintings" based on the paintings that China participated in at the London Chinese Art Exhibition. It is more than 90,000 words. He uses vivid and concise language to describe the styles, techniques, and brushwork of more than one hundred famous works from the Tang, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties, a total of one hundred and sixty-eight pieces. He also researches the origins, residences, and ranks of the artists to determine the true merits and demerits. He also critiques and lists the inscriptions and poems. For example, he wrote about Zhao Boju's "Spring Mountain Map": "...Blue and green outlines, meticulous brushstrokes, overlapping peaks and mountains, lush trees, rows of peach and willow trees, mulberry fields and grazing, Zhou Tang small boats, like a paradise, a piece of Jiangnan spring scenery; but the brushwork is immature, unlike Boju, Qian Jiang's inscription said that this frame of spirit and brushwork is consistent with Zhao Boju's true work, that is, the trial is Zhao Boju, etc., which is very incomprehensible! And carefully observe the cattle and horses and bridges in the picture, which are extremely bad, how can it be out of Boju's hand?..." He also commented on Zhao Ziang's "Double River Stacked Mountains Scroll": "...The landscape is ink, the double river is stacked with mountains, quite fortunate the meaning of the mountains and rivers are heavy, but the brushwork is soft and has no changes, the ink color is very lacking in shades, and Yongtan mostly makes pointed heads, which is both complicated and chaotic, like using cooked paper to describe, the interest is flat, and the inscriptions of celebrities of all dynasties are almost everywhere, although not Ziang's outstanding work, it is also a famous work!..." His comments are like this, and each chapter's conclusion can also be summarized and concise; and more than 30 pieces of fine and wonderful products from previous generations are selected and attached with the original image film, which is very sufficient for reference and appreciation. It is really rare in past painting records. It has been printed and published by the Commercial Press. I have the pleasure of seeing it first, so I will state the general outline to tell my friends.

On the Exquisite Rock

— Zhu Chengxi

After we reached Yu Mountain and walked west from Vimalakirti Temple, we were tired. The hard work of several days forced me to rest for a while before continuing. So we climbed onto an exquisite rock and looked at the scenery in the distance.

The Yangtze River stretched out to the southeast, its rolling waters shimmering with purple, green, ochre, and other colors in the sunlight. Patches of cloud shadows floated on the water, and the sails looked like white goose feathers. Looking down the mountainside, it was covered with red, purple, and yellow azaleas, with a riot of colors. The lakeside and fields floated on the water in squares, the rape flowers yellow and the wheat green, setting each other off, truly vivid. The wind blew, and the pine forest made a sound of pine waves, mixed with the babbling of the spring water and the singing of partridges, forming a beautiful symphony.

Looking into the distance, the hazy shadow of Wolf Mountain on the other side of the Yangtze River appeared in the smoky air, truly the so-called "spring sunshine and smoky scenery."

After sitting for a while, we regained our spirits and climbed another peak.

Breaking Bamboo Shoots

— Du Yun

A few days ago, in my hometown—Taoyuan in western Ningbo—women and girls were busy breaking bamboo shoots again. What they were breaking were "wild mountain bamboo shoots," which anyone could break without spending money. There are many kinds of bamboo shoots in our hometown. For example, mao bamboo shoots, black bamboo shoots, dragon whiskers, white shell baskets...etc., these are all private property. Each bamboo garden is surrounded by fences or low stone walls. No outsiders are allowed to dig up the bamboo shoots inside the fences and walls, otherwise they will be severely punished by the villagers. Only the wild bamboo shoots that grow in the deep mountains and cold canyons, although the mountains each have owners, the bamboo shoots are not considered private property. The kinds of bamboo shoots: the smaller ones are "flower knot full shell bamboo shoots, red shell bamboo shoots, and wild dragon whiskers." The larger ones are yellow mud bamboo shoots and wild mao bamboo shoots. Most of the ones sold in the ordinary market are private products, dug up with hoes, called digging bamboo shoots: the stems of wild mountain bamboo shoots are relatively thin, and can be broken by hand, hence the name breaking bamboo shoots.

Now that farming has started, most farmers are working in the fields, so breaking bamboo shoots is mostly done by women and girls. They decide on several comrades and set off from home in the morning. They walk vigorously into the mountains, bringing ropes and cloth. When they find a place with bamboo leaves, they rush in and break the long and short bamboo shoots, tying them into bundles with ropes. They search vigorously, crossing mountains and ridges like this. Around noon, they are hungry and tired, and they have enough bamboo shoots! Some have thirty or forty pounds, and some have ten or twenty pounds. Everyone wraps and ties them up, and leisurely comes down the mountain and returns home.

Breaking bamboo shoots once can be eaten for three to five days. If they can't finish eating them all at once, they dry the bamboo shoots or pickle them for future use. After ten days or so, they estimate that the second batch of bamboo shoots has grown up, so they invite their comrades and sisters to go again. During a bamboo shoot season, they can do this three times. But the departure date must be calculated accurately. If it is too early, the bamboo shoots have not grown out. If it is too late, they have already been broken by others. It must be just the right time to not make the trip in vain.

The taste of eating bamboo shoots is secondary, the fun of breaking them is especially strong. When I was a child, I also went with my sisters to experience it. When I occasionally recall this, I can't help but feel emotional.

A Record of What I Saw

— (Sun Choucheng)

Recently, governments in various places have been paying great attention to the word "respect for the elderly." Newspapers often report on the opening of elderly gatherings in certain provinces and cities, with grand scenes of men over 70 and women over 80 attending. Yesterday, Choucheng passed through Ximen in this city and saw a crowd gathered at the entrance of Dade Lane near the fire station. Upon closer inspection, he saw an old man with a sallow complexion and white hair, wearing a worn-out cotton-padded jacket and holding a tree branch as a walking stick, kneeling on the sidewalk. In front of him was a piece of white paper with the fourteen large characters "Most pitiful, 87-year-old bitter life, lonely and helpless." Below was written, "To the kind people in need, I am from Dingjiaji, Qingjiang. I ran a fragrance shop. Due to the drought in the fifteenth year of the Republic of China, I had nothing to say. Later, because I borrowed money from relatives, it was unlucky, and then I was robbed and burned to the ground. I came to Shanghai to seek refuge with relatives, but they looked at me differently and the money ran out due to the drought. After sleeping for half a year, it was all used up. My old wife is already 78 years old and bedridden, her life hanging by a thread. I am already 87 years old, with no sons or daughters, and no one to rely on. I am truly a bitter life. I want to go home, but I have no travel expenses. I want to go, but I can't go. I want to die, but I can't die. Therefore, I, a humble person, beg you, kind people passing by, all great benefactors, and gentlemen from all directions, to have compassion." The writing was not fluent, and the words were very sad. Some passersby threw one or two copper coins. After a while, a patrolling policeman came and told him that this place was obstructing traffic and he couldn't kneel here all the time. He ordered him to move back five steps and kneel inside the alley. To be an old man, and for happiness and bitterness to be so uneven, it is truly worthy of sighing!

Preface to "Selected Lyrics of Famous Qing Masters"

— Huang Xiaoshu

In the past, Zhu Jiangcun, a minister, often wanted to select lyrics by Qing Dynasty people for a collection of family lyrics, but he never succeeded due to procrastination. Later, in the year of Gengwu, he began to gather lyricists in Shanghai and advocated the compilation of "Qing Lyrics Copy," sending letters far and wide to search widely. He used Shanghai as the hub. I, along with Xia Chang and Chang Chang, all helped with the matter, and thus had the opportunity to see many lyric collections and understand their origins and schools. Xia Chang also compiled an estimate of the lyricists of the eleven dynasties. There were 188 people in the Shunzhi Dynasty, 117 people in the Kangxi Dynasty, 36 people in the Yongzheng Dynasty, 362 people in the Qianlong Dynasty, 328 people in the Jiaqing Dynasty, 440 people in the Daoguang Dynasty, 202 people in the Xianfeng Dynasty, 110 people in the Tongzhi Dynasty, 178 people in the Guangxu Dynasty, and 132 people in the Xuantong Dynasty. This is only based on the lyric collections seen between Geng and Xin. If we extrapolate, there are still more that were collected later and scattered in various anthologies. How prosperous! It is often said that the rise and fall of literature always depends on politics and education. Although lyrics are a minor art, one cannot reach its peak without accumulated learning, broad knowledge, and extraordinary joy and sorrow. Therefore, its origin stems from poetry, and its ability to move people is as powerful as music. The Qing Dynasty's academic prosperity surpassed the previous Ming Dynasty. During the Kangxi and Qianlong periods, the imperial examination was held twice, and talents emerged in large numbers. Most of the early Qing Dynasty lyricists were scholars, so they could develop and promote the Yuan sound. The prevailing trends gradually formed schools. Jialing vibrated in the Wu area, and Zhu Zhu was famous in Zhejiang. They were both adorned with jewels and treasures, and their qualities were equal. When Zhang Hui and others rose in the Yanghu area during the Qianlong and Jiaqing periods, they advocated the meaning within and beyond the words, and washed away the old habits of partiality. The world increasingly knew the dignity of the lyric style. Since the Tongzhi era, there have been many wars and foreign troubles. Talented and intelligent people have expressed their worries, sorrows, loyalty, love, and affectionate fragrant feelings in lyrics. The trend has become more prosperous over time. From Jiang Lutan in the distant past to Wang Bantang, Zheng Dahe, and Zhu Jiangcun in the recent past, although each is different from Yanghu, they all have the intention of mourning and devoting their hearts to the family and the country. Even if Ming Ke and other elders were resurrected in the afterlife, they could not help but fear the predecessors and younger generations. Isn't it because of the unique circumstances and unique achievements? By observing this, one can understand the changes in the world and examine the politics and education. The selection of "Qing Lyrics Copy" has already exceeded 4,000 families, but the volumes are numerous and the compilation is pending. Chen Naiqian from Haining recently carved "Selected Lyrics of Famous Qing Masters" and asked for a word. Although its selection of people is not as good as one-eleventh of "Qing Lyrics Copy," the special collections of Qing Dynasty lyricists that are truly worthy of being passed down are roughly prepared here. This is also a collection of works of a generation, and a history of customs. In the past, Song Dynasty lyric collections, such as Changsha's "Hundred Lyricists" and Fujian's "Outer Compilation of Qin Qu," were all completed in bookstores and can be examined. The Song Dynasty lyrics have been read for generations and reappear, and their survival depends on this. Chen Naiqian, in this era of literary decline, cherishes documents and continues the elegant tradition, benefiting the scholar-officials, and his achievements are very great. He should take this as a starting point to collect and publish Qing people's lyric collections as much as possible. In the year of Bingzi, April, Huang Xiaoshu of Changchang wrote in Shanghai's Jilu's Ink Play Garden.

Preface to "Selected Lyrics of Famous Qing Masters"

— Chen Naiqian

Lyric writing began in the Tang Dynasty and flourished in the Southern Song Dynasty. By the Yuan and Ming Dynasties, zaju operas arose, and lyric studies gradually declined. During the three hundred years of the Qing Dynasty, the study of scriptures and history was extremely prosperous, surpassing previous dynasties. Lyrics also suddenly revived, and their changes and outlines can be stated. Zhu Zhu and Jialing were born in the early period, reviving and revitalizing, with deep feelings and strong spirit. Fan Xie continued to echo, scrutinizing the sounds and polishing the sentences, tracing the Song Dynasty sages, and initially established the Zhejiang school's portal. However, commentators still regret that he took Jiang Zhang as the limit, biased towards physical things, and the form did not match the meaning. Its latecomers inevitably became fragmented. Therefore, the Kunling two Zhangs separately marked the meaning within and beyond the words, and Jinqing and Zhian developed and promoted it. Bantang rose, and its reality initially corresponded. Those in the countryside who viewed poetry as a minor art were suddenly enlightened to the fact that its industry was firmly on the same track as the interpretation of scriptures and poetry.

The Four Libraries of the Qing Dynasty's comprehensive collection can be described as extremely broad, but only Cao Zhenji's family was collected in the contemporary lyric collection, and only seven people were recorded. Could it be that the talents in the imperial court still regarded poetry as a minor art and despised it? However, the style of poetry flourished in the government and the opposition. Those as noble as Nalan, as rich as Yiyun, and even eccentric scholars often devoted their efforts to this, without hesitation. Among them, the changes and evolution finally reached great success. The works of expressing emotions can only be suppressed to strengthen them, and this cannot be prevented by human power.

Jiangcun's revised compilation was repeatedly proofread later, so there will be no regrets. Mr. Zhao Shuyong from Kunling edited and carved Ming lyrics, and it was more than half finished. However, Qing lyrics, which revived the traditions of the two Songs and became a great power, had no carvings. Isn't it because single volumes and isolated copies were not widely circulated, and book collectors rarely saw records? I have forgotten my poverty and humbly have ambitions for this, and I will proceed with the collection, separately edit the version, and correct it as a supplement. The rules for editing are listed on the left. I hope that the gentlemen of the Hongda family will approve it.

1. There are thousands of Qing Dynasty lyricists. First, one hundred families will be printed. After there is a collection, the second collection will be printed. This is not to say that the famous lyricists of the Qing Dynasty are limited to this.

2. The content of this compilation is all complete lyric collections. If it is only seen in anthologies, or a few lyrics are attached to the back of the poetry collection, and there is no separate collection, it will not be recorded even if it is good.

3. Ming Dynasty remnants, thinking of the old country, should be listed together with the new dynasty's officials, which is in line with the author's original intention. People like Wang Fuzhi and Qu Dajun will generally be cut off.

4. Each person's collection has several carvings. There are many or few episodes, or they are not the same. Now take them to cross-check each other to make a complete copy. For example, Wu Weiye's lyrics are combined with this collection and the family collection of Sun Mo's carvings, and Long Dingzi's lyrics are combined with this collection and Xiang Yan Su San Er Furong's lyrics. Only those who have finalized their own works in their later years will use the finalized version. For example, Wang Pengyun will use Bantang's finalized manuscript, and Zhu Guwei will use Jiangcun's language industry.

5. There are three types of punctuation marks "。" for rhymes "·" for sentences "，" for pauses. However, famous lyricists in the early Qing Dynasty followed the mistakes of Xiaoyu's score, such as the sixteen-character formula, which should now start with one character. Xiaoyu's eight scores quoted "Sleep. The moon shadows penetrate the white window, white jade money." He mistakenly used the word "sleep" for "bright," and then took the three characters "bright moon shadows" as a sentence. The punctuation often does not conform to the law. Now, only the text style is followed. I hope that those who slander will understand.

Chen Naiqian of Haining, first summer of Bingzi

Preface to "Selected Lyrics of Famous Qing Masters"

— Ye Gongchuo

I have often argued that the Qing Dynasty's scholarship surpassed the Ming Dynasty in several respects, and lyric poetry was one of them. The origins of lyric poetry began in the Tang Dynasty, flourished in the Five Dynasties, reached its peak in the Song Dynasty, and declined in the Ming Dynasty. It was not until the Qing Dynasty that it revived. Zhu and Chen guided its flow, and Shen and Li shook its waves. Zhang and Zhang occasionally talked about respecting its style, and Wang, Wen, Zheng, and Zhu continued its legacy. Talented people emerged in large numbers during the two hundred and eighty years, creating different tunes and sharing the same work, and the novelty led to differences. Even after the change of dynasties, the beautiful clouds remained. Most of today's authors are still under the influence of the Tongguang and Xuan masters. This cannot but be called a great success. However, the scattered flow of chapters and volumes needs to be reviewed and connected by wise men. For the past hundred years, there have been collections based on regional prestige, such as the Yuexi lyrics and the Huzhou lyrics records; collections based on sound and spirit, such as the Wei Province's Tong Sheng Ji and the Tijing Ji; and collections based on categories, such as the Minxiu Lyrics Copy and the Hundred Flowers Poetry Remnants. Some collections are rich in range but have not been selected, or the virtue of holding is not grand and the scale is relatively narrow. The method of collecting flowers and selecting beauty has not yet been achieved. I once edited the Qing Lyrics Copy, wanting to collect all the Qing Dynasty lyrics and select the best ones for recording. After five years of management, more than five thousand families were collected, and the work was done with caution, but it has not yet been completed. I also wanted to select the best of them as the Sixty Lyricists of Qing Dynasty, limited to those who have a definite origin and can establish their own portals. But the matter was not completed. Mr. Chen Naiqian of Haining, who inherited learning and loved the ancient, is the Jigu Pavilion of Jigu Pavilion and Zhidaozhai. Recently, he published the Qing lyrics he collected, intending to print and spread them widely, starting with a hundred families as a collection. The masters of the lyrics are roughly preserved, and the grand rules of a generation and the documents of a century are preserved, which is almost the same as what I intended. The younger generation is to be feared, and I will take the lead. When this book comes out, I will almost want to burn my pen and look at it. At this moment, the family of voices are competing and all factions are contending. I have always held the theory of adaptation, saying that in the future, new styles of songs will be created to respond to the times. However, the style and system must be inherited in order to transform, and the sincerity of the heart, the meaning, and the skills, from the inside to the outside, cannot be shaken over time. Scholars who want to know the changes and changes of this path for more than two hundred years in order to be able to obtain a teacher by themselves, then this book is in charge of its discussion. This is the preface. June of the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China, Ye Gongchuo of Panyu.

Enteritis

Enteritis is a common summer ailment. It is caused by the ingestion of spoiled food, which irritates the intestinal mucosa. Symptoms: diarrhea two or three times a day, or even thirty or forty times. Intestinal rumbling, abdominal pain, elevated body temperature, and general fatigue. Treatment: A small amount of laxative should be taken, and diarrhea should not be stopped.
